1932.10.30

Many Meetings, Little Construction, All Bad 1

Yesterday, Italian Prime Minister Mussolini delivered a speech in Milan, stating that within ten years, Fascism would spread throughout Europe, with Italy as its center. He concluded by saying that the way to restore the world's health does not lie in frequent meetings. What Italy desires is fewer meetings but more resolutions, fewer proposals but more construction.

Whether Fascism will be adopted by all of Europe within ten years, and whether Mr. Mussolini's words are entirely based on rational arguments without any exaggeration, are not what we wish to discuss today. We only feel unspeakable astonishment at the last two phrases, "fewer meetings but more resolutions, fewer proposals but more construction." In his view, it is a deeply pretentious expression. In our view, it becomes a revelation of the very core of the problem. Reading this makes one blush with shame and deep emotion. Looking around at the nations of the world, is there any country more unhealthy than our own today? Is a political situation with the most meetings and the least construction not a unique phenomenon in our country?

Let's not talk about local administration. As for the central government, there are departmental meetings, Executive Yuan meetings, Legislative Yuan meetings, National Government meetings, Central Political Council meetings, and Central Standing Committee meetings, stacked upon each other endlessly. If formal regular meetings are not enough, they are supplemented by tea parties and ad hoc meetings. Expanded versions include plenary sessions of the Central Executive Committee and national representative conferences. Added to this are the National Economic Conference,

National Internal Affairs Conference, National People's Food Conference, and various other ad hoc meetings. There is also the National Crisis Conference and special foreign affairs committees, a dazzling array too numerous to mention. The sheer number of meetings is truly astounding.

With such a constant stream of meetings, one would expect at least a few resolutions to comfort the people's eager anticipation of good governance. With such overlapping institutions, one would expect at least a prudent approach to alleviate our suffering, even if only in a small way. However, what we long for only sees the regular Yuan meetings being rehearsed day after day. Aside from reshuffling a few political personnel, there are very few resolutions that benefit the people's livelihood. As for slightly difficult events, the Yuan refers them to the Central Political Council, which refers them to the Central Standing Committee. If the Central Standing Committee still cannot decide, they gather various Central Committee members to exchange opinions and widely solicit views. If they still cannot decide, the matter is left for the plenary session of the Central Executive Committee to decide, or directly returned to the original agency for reconsideration. The report goes up and is sent back down, resulting in extremely tortuous results. The crux of the problem may not be fully resolved. Resolutions are so difficult to obtain. As for construction, whenever a major conference is convened, talented individuals gather. Discussions flow like springs, and proposals are loaded by the cartload. The postal and telegraph services are exhausted from delivery, and newspapers struggle to cover everything. Then, we hear that the proposals have been organized, submitted for review, discussed, shelved, revised and passed, and handed over to the government for implementation. Finally, the conference closes. Once the conference closes, our hopes also come to an end. Empty mountains, no people seen, only the sound of voices heard, is a true reflection of our country's meetings.

What we find particularly strange is that the committee members attending various meetings mostly have overlapping roles. For example, many members of the Foreign Affairs Committee are also members of the Central Political Council. To say that an event that the Foreign Affairs Committee cannot resolve can be resolved by the Central Political Council, or that an opinion that cannot be contributed in the Central Political Council can be expressed in the Foreign Affairs Committee, is not this a ridiculous and laughable matter? Government officials, usually unprepared for any contingencies, resort to propaganda as a shield when faced with urgent situations and public criticism. Today, Committee Member A releases a statement saying that a certain case has been resolved. Tomorrow, Important Person B issues a statement saying that a certain matter has a correct plan. They only aim for immediate peace and quiet, disregarding factual proof. This is like the monkey keeper's trick of four in the morning and three in the evening. The effectiveness of meetings is becoming increasingly limited.

In short, if there are many meetings but no resolutions, it is better not to meet. If there are many proposals but no construction, it is better not to propose. Without meetings and proposals, we might still hope to solve difficult problems through meetings and carry out construction according to proposals one day. If we are in meetings every day, and no progress can be seen, if there is an abundance of speech, but no one takes responsibility, if we plan buildings without success, how far are we from restoring health? Mr. Mussolini's words can be used as a source of inspiration for improvement. The evening drum and morning bell awaken deep reflection in the gentlemen of the government. Listen carefully, listen carefully.

Important Telegrams

Shandong Affairs Have Been Resolved 2

Jiang Bocheng Arrives in Jinan, Fruitful Results from Further Consultations with Han

The Third Route Army Decides to Complete Withdrawal by the 8th; Yantai and Longkou Temporarily Return to Naval Defense

Jiang, Xiong, and Gao Supervise the Withdrawal of Troops by Both Sides; The Location Where Liu's Troops Will be Transferred is Undecided

(Jinan) At 9:00 AM this morning, Jiang Bocheng arrived in Jinan. Han and other important figures welcomed him at the station. After Jiang disembarked, he went to the Jiaoji Hotel with Han to discuss solutions for Jiaodong with Zhang Fang. In the morning, He Yingqin's reply telegram arrived in Jinan, leading to further consultations with satisfactory results, and everyone was delighted. Jiang told reporters: 1. The withdrawal of the First and Third Route Armies is overdue. Han requested a delay of several days. Minister He replied in a telegram that as long as General Xiang Fang could withdraw the Third Route Army west of the Weifang River, a slight delay of a few days would be acceptable. It has now been agreed with Han that the withdrawal will be completed by August 8th. 2. Yantai and Longkou will temporarily return to the defense of the Northeast Navy to facilitate the transfer of Liu's troops from these two locations. 3. In addition to Fushan, Muping, Qixia, Laiyang, and Ye County, where Liu's troops will temporarily be stationed, the Third Route Army will leave a small number of troops in Wendeng, Rongcheng, Penglai, Huang County, Zhaoyuan, Haiyang, and Pingdu to maintain order together with the Shandong local militia because of the existing bandits. 4. The Central Government has sent me, Xiong Bin, and Gao Lingbai to supervise the withdrawal and transfer of troops by both sides. I plan to ask Xiong to go to Ye County, Gao to Yantai, and I will stay in Jinan. 5. After the Third Route Army completes its withdrawal on the 8th, an order will be issued to transfer Liu away from Shandong. The destination is unknown. In this way, the prestige of the central government and the suffering of the local people can both be taken into account. This matter can be considered resolved. Gao has arrived in Jinan, but Xiong has not yet come. Zhang Fang plans to go to Qingdao tomorrow. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Jinan) The entire Shandong provincial government committee and the secretary-general hosted a banquet at the People's Hall for Jiang Bocheng and Zhang Fang. Han said that the Third Route Army would withdraw to the Pingdu and Changyi area. Liu's troops were being driven out by local governments and people. If I were in Liu's position, I would have asked to leave voluntarily. The areas within 20-30 miles of Laiyang and the city gates of Ye County have been severely damaged by Liu's troops, and the provincial government will have to assist in their recovery in the future. The port of Yantai is excellent, and if the population is about the same, it will not be difficult to compete with Qingdao after proper reorganization. I believe that the central government should first assist in unifying provincial administrations in various provinces, and then the central government will be unified. Han decided to personally visit Chiang in Wuhan and request punishment after the Jiaodong matter is resolved. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Liu Zhennian's representative, Liu Yiru, went to Tianjin this afternoon to handle important official business. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Yu Xuezhong sent a representative, Li Jun, to Shandong to mediate the Jiaodong war. Li passed through Tianjin on the morning of the 29th en route to Beiping. Reportedly, Han stated that if Liu's army leaves Shandong, he will immediately withdraw his troops. It is estimated that the entire matter can be resolved in another week. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Although the Central Government is making every effort to reconcile the Shandong dispute, it is reported that fierce fighting continues in Laizhou (formerly Ye County). According to a telegram from a foreigner in Yantai, Liu Zhennian and several thousand of his troops are still defending Laizhou. Another 500 are defending Qixia. A hundred of Han's cavalry have appeared outside the city. Liu's army is currently engaged in raids in the Laiyang area to obtain food and clothing. Yantai is peaceful. One Chinese warship is anchored in the harbor, along with British, American, and Japanese warships. (29th Reuters Telegram)

The Black Citadel May Fall in the Evening Amidst the Encirclement of Righteous Armies 3

Undercover Teams Inside the City Are Very Active

Zhang Dianjiu's Army Reaches the Opposite Bank of the Nen River

(Harbin) Although the Japanese army and Fu Zhaolin are likely to reach an agreement, the Northeast Righteous Armies have formed a siege around Heihe, advancing on Heihe from the north from Heihe, from the south from the Nen River, and from the west from Fularji. The contact between Ma Zhanshan, Su Bingwen, and Li Haiqing is very close. Undercover teams inside Heihe are very active, and leaflets denouncing the Japanese and traitors are found everywhere. Public morale is shaken, and many in the puppet army are responding in a timely manner. Upon hearing this news, the Japanese have been conferring daily to discuss countermeasures. Heihe is in imminent danger. (29th China United Press Telegram)

A portion of Zhang Dianjiu's army from Qiqihar, about 500 men, suddenly appeared on the opposite bank of the Nen River outside Qiqihar, preparing to cross the river and advance on Qiqihar. The Japanese army deployed artillery at the old airfield outside the west gate and began shelling Zhang's army at 4:00 PM on the 27th. (29th Dentsu Telegram)

(Beiping) A person from Manchuria reported that since Su Bingwen launched his campaign in Hailar on the 28th of last month, he has completely monitored the Japanese residents in Hailar and Manchuria. The Japanese military authorities, unaware of the truth, sent someone to Hailar secretly to persuade him, but Su sternly refused. Recently, Japanese planes have been scattering threatening leaflets in the Hailar-Manchuria area, but the National Salvation Army is not paying much attention because they were prepared. Su personally swore an oath in Hailar, declaring his determination to recover the territory, and secretly sent representatives to various places to contact Ma Zhanshan and the Heilongjiang army, agreeing on a date for a general offensive. As the military situation of various armies is making progress, the Japanese have begun to understand that Su's army is fighting against Japan, and they have urgently deployed Matsuki Tadaaki's 14th Division to Heilongjiang. For the sake of long-term resistance, Su's army has built defenses in the large mountains along the Chinese Eastern Railway line from Zhalantun to Hailar, with extremely careful arrangements. (29th Special Dispatch)

Feng Zhanhai's Troops Attack Changchun 4

(Beiping) Feng Zhanhai is leading over ten thousand troops to advance towards Changchun, and he is connecting with the work teams previously in the vicinity of Changchun to launch a major offensive against Changchun. They have reached the Hailaha Guobaoshan Shitong area, about 200 miles from Changchun. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Feng Zhanhai telegraphed Beiping stating that his troops are still in the Kailu area of Jilin, and their strength has been replenished. He will soon lead his troops to attack Jilin for the second time. (29th Special Dispatch)

The Righteous Army in Taonan Comes into Contact with Japanese Soldiers 5

(Beiping) Sixty miles outside the city of Taonan, the Righteous Army is occasionally coming into contact with Japanese soldiers. On the evening of the 16th, the Taonan River suddenly rose sharply. Over two hundred Japanese soldiers attempted to block the flood, but the dike was breached due to the overwhelming force of the water. The Japanese soldiers who were trying to control the flood narrowly escaped drowning. Over twenty villages were affected, and all of the houses were destroyed. (29th Special Dispatch)

The Japanese Army Provokes at Chaoyang Temple 6

(Beiping) Japanese armored vehicles have been shelling the Chaoyang Temple area for days, provoking a response. Japanese Captain Oohashi claimed that this was to suppress the Righteous Army. Japanese planes are constantly scouting over Beipiao and Chaoyang. Our Cui Brigade is holding its ground at the front, and the Japanese have not dared to attack lightly. However, supplies are lacking, and the Rehe authorities hope for assistance from all sides. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) After the Japanese army's intrusion into Nanling and Liulongtai on the 10th failed, Meng Zhaoyan's troops of the Righteous Army stationed near Yixian seized the opportunity to recapture Chaoyang Temple and occupy the railway station. Later, the Japanese army launched a counterattack with armored vehicles, resulting in fierce fighting. The Japanese army, due to the high mountains and steep ridges between Nanling and Koubeiyingzi, abandoned its plan to invade Rehe along the Jinzhou-Chaoyang Road. Recently, the Japanese army has been using several thousand Mongolian troops from Tongliao to attempt to create disturbances. Cui Xingwu, the brigade commander of the Rehe army stationed in Kailu, is actively defending and contacting Feng Zhanhai's troops to guard the Rehe border. Defenses are solid. Japanese planes are constantly scattering leaflets and dropping bombs. Kailu and Chaoyang are peaceful. (29th Special Dispatch)

Two Brigades of the Soviet Army Join Forces to Attack Ningnian 7

(Beiping) Su Bingwen telegraphed from Hailar on the 27th, stating that Pu Binghuan led infantry to the western end of the Yaoxing Village, west of the Taianzhen, and suddenly encountered the enemy, consisting of about 300 soldiers and cavalry with two cannons. Fierce fighting broke out, killing over 30 enemies, and the enemy retreated. They returned the next day but were beaten back after we fiercely struck them, killing more than 10 and they fled in disarray, using the Babeizi Palace as a stronghold. That Mongol accepted the Japanese and opposed us, harboring the Japanese army. Otherwise, we would have completely annihilated the enemy on the 15th. We captured many enemy machine guns, rifles, and military supplies in the last two days, and we will completely resolve that fort in one or two days, making a long drive forward. Our Sa Brigade is near Fuhai, and He Brigade is advancing towards Minnian. Li Zhenhua Brigade has already contacted us and will join in attacking Ningnian. Morale is extremely high among both the military and the people. (29th Special Dispatch)

Japanese Women in Manzhouli Have Left the Country 8

(Harbin) According to Japanese newspaper reports, all Japanese women and children in Manzhouli have left the country and entered Russian territory, but the Japanese military authorities have not yet received confirmation of this report. (29th Reuters Telegram) (Tokyo) Regarding the rescue of the Japanese who have been detained in Manzhouli, the military has been unable to contact Su Bingwen and has negotiated with the Russian government, requesting that it send a negotiator and provide various conveniences for the negotiator. On the 27th, Russia fully accepted Japan's request and decided to send several negotiators from the Kwantung Army, assisted by Major Yamaoka Michitake, an adjutant infantry officer stationed in Moscow, and Russian officials, to negotiate exclusively with Su Bingwen to rescue all the detained Japanese. Although the military hopes for a peaceful resolution, it is determined to use force as a last resort if Su continues to maintain his anti-Manchuria and anti-Japanese stance. (29th Dentsu Telegram)

Liu Xiang's Troops Reportedly Occupy Yongchuan 9

Sichuan Generals to Issue Joint Telegram

Dai Shi Drafts Settlement Plan

(Nanjing) A telegram from Chongqing states: 1. The local authorities here will jointly telegram the central government. It will be led by Liu Xiang, followed by Tian Songyao, Deng Xihou, Yang Sen, Liu Cunhou, and others. According to the telegrams previously issued by the generals outlining methods to resolve the Sichuan situation, they request that the central government adopt these methods immediately so that the disasters of war can be relieved. 2. The joint army stationed in Shunqing is gradually expanding westward. The affairs of Shunqing and other counties are being taken over by the war zone committee. 3. The fighting in Rongchang on the 28th was fierce, but the details are not yet clear. Two battalions of the 24th Army were surrounded in eastern Rongchang. 4. The 21st Army, led by Pan Wenhua, captured Jiangjin on the 26th. Most of the 24th Army was stationed at Tai'an Chang, near Yongchuan. On the 27th, they were defeated by the 21st Army, which is about to completely occupy Yongchuan. 5. The generals in Chongqing have jointly nominated Liu Xiang as the commander-in-chief of the Sichuan-Kangsu pacification army and Tian Songyao as the deputy. Deng Xihou, Tian Songyao, Yang Sen, and Liu Xiang have been nominated as the commanders of the first, second, third, and fourth route armies, and they are preparing to issue a joint telegram taking office. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) A telegram from Chengdu states that Tian Songyao has telegraphed Liu Xiang, asking him to go to Suining for a meeting to implement the proposals in the telegrams from the generals. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Central Political Council has appointed Dai Fu'xian and Shi Qingyang to negotiate a resolution to the Sichuan issue. Dai and Shi have exchanged opinions several times and have drafted a settlement plan, which will be submitted to the Central Political Council for discussion next Wednesday. It is said that the proposed plan calls for all armies to cease hostilities immediately and reorganize the Sichuan provincial government. If the two Lius and the various armies agree, the central government will send personnel to Sichuan to convene a meeting of all armies to seek a thorough resolution. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Nanjing office of the 24th Army issued a telegram from Chengdu on the 29th: 1. The Lai regiment of the 24th Army has abandoned Jiangjin and retreated to the Baisha Hejiang area, uniting various units to prepare for a field battle. 2. Fierce fighting broke out between the 24th and 21st Armies at Chadian Tai'an Shimiao, Yongchuan Front, from the 28th, and both sides have suffered many casualties. They are still holding their positions. 3. Yang Sen arrived in Suining on the 27th and telegraphed Deng and Tian, asking them to meet in Suining. There will be new developments in the Sichuan War. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Liu Wenhui telegraphed his representative in Nanjing, Leng Rong, on the 28th, stating that he has voluntarily abandoned Shunqing, Suishang, Tongnan, Jiangjin, and other counties to avoid the complete ruin of the overall situation. As for the defense of Xikang, he is determined to be responsible to the end and will not send a single soldier back east to participate in the civil war. He hopes to convey this message to the people from Kangzang in Nanjing. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Wu Peifu repeatedly telegraphed Deng Xihou and Yang Sen, asking them to mediate the Sichuan War. Deng replied to Wu, stating that mediation of the Sichuan War was ineffective and difficult to resolve with laughter or tears. Yang also sent a reply to Beiping, agreeing to try to persuade them. (29th Special Dispatch)

He Chengjun Convenes a Meeting of Generals in Fancheng 10

(Hankou) He Chengjun has been convening meetings in Fancheng for several days with Wei Lihuang, Liu Maoen, Zhu Huaibing, Liu Ji, and other military and political figures to discuss methods for suppressing bandits and providing relief. He will go to Laohekou within days to supervise the troops. Personnel from He's office, led by Yang Yadong, will go to Fancheng, and personnel from the Department of Civil Affairs will also depart with them. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) Wei Lihuang telegraphed that Xu Xiangqian's remaining bandits were defeated by the Jiang and Li divisions. Jiang's division reportedly killed over a thousand bandits, and the puppet regimental commander was killed in battle. The commander and political commissar of the puppet 11th Division were seriously injured. Li's division killed two thousand bandits, captured over three hundred, and seized many weapons. The remaining bandits fled north, numbering less than four thousand. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Liang Guanying telegraphed that in the bandit suppression campaign at Longjing Pass, the puppet regimental commander, Shi Qibo, was killed, and the bandit troops of the puppet Eastern Route Army Commander Liu Shiqi, numbering over four thousand, were routed. Many were captured. (29th Special Dispatch)

Legislative Yuan Passes the International Convention for the Safety of Life at Sea 11

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan held its 208th meeting at 8:00 AM on the 29th. Thirty-nine members were present, including Luo Ding, with Chairman Shao Yuanchong representing the President and Zhang Weihan as Secretary-General. The agenda included: (1) A case submitted by the Central Political Council regarding the amendment of five principles in the Provisional Law on Supervising Local Finances. Resolved: referred to the Finance and Economic Committees for review. (2) The Foreign Affairs Committee of the Legislative Yuan reported that it had jointly reviewed the International Convention for the Safety of Life at Sea and its subsidiary rules with committee members Zhu Hezhong, Wei Tingsheng, and Shi Weihuan. Resolved: Passed. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The International Convention for the Safety of Life at Sea was initiated by Germany, Austria, Belgium, Canada, Denmark, Spain, Estonia, the United States, the United Kingdom, Finland, France, India, Italy, Japan, Norway, the Netherlands, Switzerland, and other countries, and was signed in London on May 31, 1929. The Chinese government has not yet joined. The Legislative Yuan passed the full text of the convention, consisting of 66 articles and 53 attachments, at its 208th meeting on the 29th. (29th Special Dispatch)

Chiang Arrives in Changsha by Ship 12

(Changsha) President Chiang, accompanied by his wife Soong Mei-ling and others, arrived in Changsha at 2:00 PM on the 29th aboard the Jiangkun warship. He Jian and others boarded a boat to welcome him. After Chiang disembarked, he nodded in greeting to those welcoming him. The people along the way cheered. He then took a car to the headquarters to rest. Various party, government, and military figures visited him. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Changsha) Chiang boarded the Chuyou and Weisheng warships in Wuhan on the 27th to inspect Hunan. His wife Soong Mei-ling and 13 staff members accompanied him. He arrived in Yuezhou at noon on the 28th and went ashore to visit the mountains. At 3:00 PM, he transferred to the Jiangxi and Jiangkun warships and sailed upstream. He stayed overnight in Zhaozhou on the 28th. Due to the shallow water, it was not convenient to travel at night. He arrived in Changsha at the designated time on the 29th. (29th Special Dispatch)

Case of Chen Duxiu is Heard in Beijing Investigative Court 13

(Nanjing) The Jiangsu High Court dispatched Prosecutor Zhu Jun and clerks to Beijing to hold a hearing at the Second Criminal Court of the Jiangning Court this morning at 9:30 to investigate the criminal case of Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi. The hearing adjourned at 11:00. Prosecutor Zhu is still staying in Beijing and will hold another hearing next Monday before returning to Jiangsu to file a public prosecution. Zhu stated that due to the seriousness of the case, the prison has been instructed to refuse all visitors and correspondence during the investigation. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) After Communist Party members Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi were handed over to the Jiangning District Court, the court reported to the Jiangsu High Court. It is reported that the Jiangsu High Court will soon send a prosecutor to Beijing to hold an investigative hearing to clarify the evidence of the crime before filing a lawsuit. Then, the Jiangsu High Court will send a judge to Beijing to hold a public trial. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Lin Biao, the President of the Jiangsu High Court, came to Beijing on the 29th to hear the case of Chen Duxiu and Peng Jinzhi and to meet with the authorities of the Ministry of Justice to discuss all matters. (29th Special Dispatch)

Masterminds of the Jiangdu Tax Revolt Executed by Firing Squad 14

(Yangzhou) Ge Guangxing, Chen Youshan, Luo Cailiang, Yang Dechang, Liu Yushan, and Bu Dengyun, the masterminds of the tax revolt, were executed by firing squad on the 29th. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Zhenjiang) After an investigation by the Henan and Li provincial committees into the Yangzhou tax revolt, the key criminals Ge Guangxing, Chen Youshan, Luo Cailiang, Yang Dechang, Liu Yushan, and Bu Dengyun were executed by firing squad on the morning of the 29th. In the proclamation of their crimes, it was stated that Ge and others had confessed to colluding with bandits and communists to take advantage of the situation and create chaos, so they were severely punished. However, other villagers who followed them would not be held deeply responsible. Yang Zhuomao, the county magistrate of Jiangdu, left Yangzhou on the 29th, and county affairs are being handled by the secretary on his behalf. (29th Special Dispatch)

Railway to Construct Sun Yat-sen Wharf 15

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Railways plans to use the Dengping Wharf in Xiaguan for the Jinpu ferry exclusively for cargo, while passengers will be transported by the Sun Yat-sen Wharf. Bids were invited on the 29th to contract out all construction work for the Sun Yat-sen Wharf. (29th Central News Agency Telegram)

Military Academy Students Prepare to Travel 16

(Nanjing) Students of the Central Military Academy are scheduled to travel to Baohua Mountain on November 1st, 3rd, and 6th. Students of the Army University are also scheduled to travel to Danyang and Zhenjiang soon and conduct field exercises. The Ministry of Railways has been notified to provide free transportation. (29th Central News Agency Telegram)

Chen Jiliang Inspects Warships Stationed in Nanjing 17

(Nanjing) Chen Jiliang arrived in Nanjing on the 27th after inspecting the warships stationed in Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and Anhui. He inspected the Haichou and Yongsheng warships on the 28th and the Jing'an and Ding'an warships on the 29th. There are still over ten warships awaiting inspection, including the new Ninghai warship. Since the warship arrived in Nanjing, many people from all walks of life have visited it. However, due to its participation in the inspection, visits have been temporarily suspended. (29th Central News Agency Telegram)

Nanjing Expands Sanitary Services 18

(Nanjing) The Nanjing Municipal Health Office has been reorganized through cooperation between the municipal government and the Ministry of Health. The reorganization, which was passed by the municipal government meeting, will be implemented on the 1st of next month. The current director, Chen Pu, has resigned, and Wang Zuxiang, the chief of the Medical Administration Section of the Ministry of Health, will take over. (29th Special Dispatch)

Geological Research Institute Proceeds with Work 19

(Nanjing) Li Siguang, Director of the Geological Research Institute of Academia Sinica, has been actively working recently, using the latest torsion balance to measure the gravity of Nanjing's subsurface. He has also invited many geological experts to form groups and go out to conduct research. Experts Ye Liangfu and Yu Deyuan have already gone to Anhui to research the Shangyao mines in Shungeng Mountain, Huaiyuan County. Meng Xianmin and Zhang Geng will soon go to the Mantou Mountain and other places in Guichi County, southern Anhui, to study the origin and structure of coalfield geology. Li Yuyao and Li Zhang

Page 4

Zhu Sen and others will travel to various provinces in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River to study mountain structures and the origins of rivers. (29th Special Dispatch)

Various Ministries and Commissions Rush to Prepare Work Reports 20

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan, with the Third Plenary Session approaching, ordered all subordinate ministries and commissions to report on all political work since the close of the Second Plenary Session, classified by category, in order to compile a general report for submission to the conference. (29th Special Dispatch)

Metropolitan Police Seizes Opium 21

(Nanjing) The Metropolitan Police Yijiangmen Inspection Office found it suspicious when an Asia Petroleum Company truck carrying gasoline entered the city on the 29th. Twelve bags of opium, weighing over 1,500 taels, were found on the spot, and the opium trafficker, surnamed Luo, was detained and sent to the Judicial Section for questioning. (29th Special Dispatch)

First Meeting of the Jiangsu People's Food Association 22

(Zhenjiang) The Jiangsu-Nanjing-Shanghai People's Food Association held its first committee meeting on the 29th. More than ten people attended, including Jiang Wenyu. Qian Sunqing chaired the meeting. The following resolutions were made: (1) Huang Renzhi, Mu Ouchu, Jiang Wenyu, Lu Xiaobo, Yu Xiaochuan, Yang Hanxi, and Qian Sunqing were elected as standing committee members. (2) To promote public warehouses, the work will be divided into four groups: A. The Jiangsu Business Federation will be responsible for ten counties including Yanggao, Baoxing, Taidong, etc.; B. The Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce and the Provincial Agricultural Bank will be responsible for six counties including Zhenjiang, Dantu, Julu, Licun, etc.; C. The Wuxi and Liangxi Chambers of Commerce will be responsible for nine counties including Zhenjiang, Changshu, Kun, etc.; D. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Land Association will be responsible for three counties including Songjiang, Qingpu, and Jinshan. (29th Special Telegram)

Forbidden City Prepares to Open for Eight Days 23

(Beiping) Eight cultural institutions, including the Palace Museum, the Institute of Historical Philology of Academia Sinica, etc., will jointly open for eight days starting from the sixth of next month to raise money for winter clothing to relieve the disaster in the Northeast. Yu Xuezhong Arrives in Beiping to Meet Zhang 24

(Beiping) Yu Xuezhong arrived in Beiping yesterday. According to reports, he came to discuss the political situation in Hebei Province and plans to report to Zhang. He is scheduled to meet with Zhang tonight and will return to Tianjin tonight or tomorrow morning. The jointly operated government-business Hebei Mining Company is scheduled to open on the first of next month. Recently, a large group of bandits was discovered near the coastal Gege and Jinghai areas. Troops were dispatched to suppress them severely. The bandits near Gege have been cleared, and the bandit leader Liu Er Waibo has been arrested. The remaining bandits have fled, and the provincial army is pursuing them along the coast. The communist bandits in Li County have been eliminated, and their leaders have been arrested. (29th Special Telegram)

They will first go to Jining County and are scheduled to return to Sui together next month. In the vicinity of Suizhong, a large group of bandits has been discovered for more than a month. They have kidnapped more than 600 men and women as hostages in recent days, claiming that the ransom money will be used to purchase cotton clothing. (29th Special Telegram)

Communist Criminals from Huaiyin Escorted to Zhenjiang 38

Foreign News

Japanese Opinion on Lytton Report Transported to China 40

Including Appendices, Packed in Three Large Boxes

To be Delivered to the National Government by Minister Arima

▲ Hualian News Agency, Tokyo, 29th: Japan's opinion on the Lytton Report and 76 types of related documents are packed, sealed into three boxes, and shipped to Shanghai today by Nagasaki Maru to Minister Arima, who will then deliver it to the National Government.

Hualian News Agency, Tokyo, 29th: Ambassador Yoshida, carrying the opinion on the Lytton Report, departed from Tokyo Station on the night of the 28th via Siberia to Geneva. Before his departure, he expressed the following opinions to reporters at Tokyo Station: Regarding the Manchurian problem, there are various speculations, but in reality, one cannot be optimistic or pessimistic. The League of Nations will inevitably use the report as a basis for handling the Sino-Japanese dispute. However, it cannot be easily resolved in either the Council or the General Assembly. Regardless of the various discussions on the report, it cannot be discarded. In short, Japan must use its advantageous points, such as the report containing the complex situation in Manchuria and the historical background, which has caused British representative Sir Cecil to change his attitude. Therefore, the Council will not dare to regard Japan as an aggressor as before. As for Japan's position in Manchuria, it is argued that there are special political and economic circumstances, which no other country in the world has. Japan must not lightly overlook such impractical theories. Furthermore, Lytton himself has recognized that Chapters Nine and Ten of the report need to be changed in the face of the ever-changing situation. Therefore, the Council cannot but fully consider this point. As for the description of the September 18th Incident and the establishment of "Manchukuo," our country will resolutely not recognize them. The launch of our right of self-defense can be explained in detail. The establishment of "Manchukuo" is based on the self-determination of 30 million people, which goes without saying. A survey team that only stayed in Manchuria for six weeks, of course, cannot observe correctly. I can arrive in Geneva on the 14th. If I cannot make it in time, the opinion may be transported by plane first, it is said.

▲ Havas, Berlin, 28th: In February of last year, a communist worker was arrested for stealing industrial secrets and selling them to the Soviet Union. New evidence has been obtained regarding the German chemical plant's manufacturing of military supplies. According to Article 171 of the Treaty of Versailles, "All asphyxiating, poisonous or other gases, and all analogous liquids, materials or devices are prohibited, the manufacture and importation of which are therefore strictly forbidden in Germany. The equipment specially designed for the manufacture, storage or use of the said articles or devices shall also be strictly forbidden."

Japanese Communist Party Case, After 128 Court Sessions, is Adjudicated 45

185 Defendants

Sentenced to Varying Terms of Imprisonment

▲ Reuters, Tokyo, 29th: Japan's large-scale arrest of communists four years ago has finally been adjudicated today. A total of 185 people have been sentenced. Four people have been sentenced to life imprisonment, including Sano, who was arrested in Shanghai three years ago. Fourteen people have been sentenced to imprisonment for ten to fifteen years, and the rest have also been sentenced to imprisonment for terms ranging from two to nine years. When the presiding judge handed down the sentence, he said that the Japanese Communist Party is a branch of the Third International, and the defendants have all engaged in revolutionary struggles, aiming to establish a labor dictatorship.

▲ Dentsu News Agency, Tokyo, 29th: The sentencing of 185 members of the Second Communist Party, which has undergone 128 trials since June of last year, was pronounced by Judge Miyagi at the Tokyo District Court at 9:00 am today. At that time, the courthouse was heavily guarded by 300 armed police and 150 military police. The 60 spectator tickets were monopolized by right-wing groups such as the Patriotic Student League. The defendants looked back at the spectator seats, seemingly surprised. During the sentencing, the defendants were divided into groups A and B. Group A was sentenced in the morning, and Group B was sentenced in the afternoon. Except for the 26 people whose sentences were suspended, the others were all sentenced to imprisonment. Those who were severely punished are as follows: Party Central Committee Chairman Sano Manabu, life imprisonment; Party Central Committee member and Central Union Minister Nabe Osada Chika, life imprisonment; Party Central Committee member and Hokkaido Local Committee Chairman Mitamura Shiro, death penalty; Party Central Committee member and Executive Committee Chairman Ichikawa Shoichi, life imprisonment; Party Central Committee member Fukumoto Kazuo, ten years imprisonment; Party Central Committee members Sugiura Keiichi and Kawada Kenji, both imprisoned for ten years (as requested by the prosecutor); Takahashi Sadae and Kuninryo Goichiro, both sentenced to fifteen years imprisonment (according to the prosecutor's request).

New Legal Disarmament Plan 46

Advocates German Dissolution of Defense Forces

As a Condition for Acknowledging Reduction of Conscription

International Treaties of Mutual Assistance Should Be Concluded

Disputes Must Be Subject to Compulsory Arbitration

▲ National News Agency, Paris, 28th: France's new security and disarmament plan, which includes important proposals from several countries, was discussed in the National Assembly today. After Herriot explained in detail, it was passed by a vote of 430 to 20. It includes a general disarmament consultation convention, which is expected to be signed by the United States as well. In addition, there are several conventions, all concerning the control of local mutual assistance armaments. There is also a plan to organize an international air force under the management of the League of Nations. However, France's overall plan only outlines the main points, and the detailed plan is still to be discussed. As for Germany's demand for equal armaments, Herriot advocated for negotiating a record of the meeting to recognize it in principle, but mutual concessions are required. Germany should also abolish its defense forces in exchange for France further reducing military service. He believes that with the proposed conventions as a guarantee, this point should not be difficult to resolve satisfactorily. If international disputes arise, then according to the French plan, compulsory arbitration must be used. In addition, Herriot also advocated for establishing a permanent international committee to conduct on-site investigations of armaments in various countries. The committee should have full power to conduct investigations and, if it finds any obvious violations, report them to the League of Nations, it is said.

▲ Havas, Paris, 28th: The French government has recently released a summary of the outline of the plan for disarmament and security. The main idea is that France acknowledges shortening the term of military service and making it universal from a certain period, subject to the following conditions: (1) All armed groups, such as the German defense forces, whose terms of service are longer, should be regarded as domestic police forces and suppressed; (2) An international inspection system should be established, which must include the right of search; (3) Local mutual assistance treaties should be concluded between countries to supplement the deficiencies of the Locarno Treaty, so that all European countries can participate in the guarantee of peace and make the international community have sufficient public force to prevent acts of aggression. This international force should include the first batch of troops, jointly composed of teams specially trained for this purpose by various countries. This force can be dispatched immediately in case of emergency and is equipped with the strongest armaments; (4) The United States should also provide security guarantees, the method of which should be considered by the country itself; (5) All member states of the League of Nations should acknowledge and fulfill all obligations stipulated in Article 16 of the Covenant; (6) All those who acknowledge mutual assistance treaties should accept compulsory arbitration.

US Representative Davis Arrives in Paris 47

Reconciling Continental Countries' Opinions on Disarmament

▲ Havas, Paris, 28th: US disarmament representative Davis arrived in Paris from London at 5:45 pm.

▲ Havas, London, 28th: Semi-official sources believe that the result of the negotiations between US representative Davis and the British authorities is only to clarify the proposals of the three signatory countries of the London Naval Treaty. This is evidenced by the somewhat vague declaration of US representative Davis. Therefore, in reality, these negotiations have not achieved any current effect, and the Japanese proposal, which is still secret, does not seem to simplify the problem. Furthermore, the elements of the naval problem are not only in the mutual views of the UK, US, and Japan. Davis's intention is to pay particular attention to the opinions of the continental countries on this problem. It is recalled that when the London Naval Conference was held in 1930, the opinions of the continental countries could not be reconciled, especially between France and Italy, which the United States deeply regretted. Some people therefore believe that Davis may come to the UK again after visiting the continent.

Disarmament Leaders to Meet at the Beginning of Next Month 48

First Review Three Reports

▲ Havas, Geneva, 28th: The presidium of the Disarmament Conference decided to meet on November 3rd and issued invitations tonight. The agenda will begin with a report by Chairman Henderson on the general situation of disarmament work, followed by a review of the reports by Belgian representative Bourquin, Italian representative Pilotti, and Spanish representative on tanks (prepared by Uruguayan representative Piro). The first three reports have been studied by the presidium. Belgian representative Bourquin's report studies the powers of the Armaments Supervisory Committee and the organizational and operational conditions of such supervision. The Italian representative's report advocates for the establishment of a special supervisory committee to be responsible for studying the manufacturing of chemicals specifically for military use. From this, it can be seen that the Italian representative's report is more detailed than the Belgian representative's report, because Bourquin only proposed working methods, while Pilotti reached a conclusion. The report of the Spanish representative Madariaga studies air armaments, but only re-examines the problem of supervising civilian aircraft that can be used for aerial bombing. He intends to provide adequate protection to civilians from the danger of aerial bombing, so he advocates for supervising civilian aviation to prevent it from being converted for military use.

Proposals to Ban Chemical Warfare 49

▲ National News Agency, Geneva, 28th: Italian representative Pilotti today submitted several proposals regarding the implementation of a ban on various chemical, incendiary, and bacteriological warfare to Disarmament Conference Chairman Henderson. The proposals first prohibit preparations during peacetime, such as manufacturing such materials and issuing usage instructions. Then, a chemical group should be established within the Permanent Disarmament Committee and given full power to deal with violators. If a country is accused of violating the agreement, it will go to the site for investigation. If it is indeed true, sanctions will be imposed. Regarding the method of sanctions, one provision allows for pressure to be applied to the violating country, first ordering it to abandon the prohibited weapons and depriving it of the possibility of continuing to use them. Then, the countries will negotiate punitive methods and send suggestions and prohibitions to the warring countries. The final step is to allow the victim country to retaliate, but its scope of use must not exceed the actual conflict area.

International Telegraph Conference Special Committee Passes Draft Inspection Clause 50

▲ National News Agency, Madrid, 28th: The International Transportation Conference Special Committee passed a new draft of the telegram inspection clause proposed by the US representative today. The clause is Article 25 of the original agreement, stipulating that the signatory governments reserve the right to stop the transmission of wired and wireless communications that are deemed to endanger national security, violate public order laws, and be contrary to etiquette. However, if transmission is stopped, the originating telegraph station should be notified immediately, except when such notification would endanger national security. The US representative believes that this provision can adequately protect government rights and public interests. Representatives from China, Japan, Czechoslovakia, and Austria advocated for expanding the scope of inspection and proposed amendments, but the committee deemed it unnecessary to expand and did not adopt them.

▲ National News Agency, Paris, 29th: This morning, the National Assembly expressed its confidence in the Herriot government by a vote of 430 to 20 and passed a resolution expressing friendly sentiments towards the Spanish Republic before adjourning.

Foreign News Three

The World's Rural Plight, US Grain Bins Overflowing 52

Wheat Prices are the Lowest in Centuries

Farmers are Even Using it as Fuel

▲ National News Agency, Washington, 28th: While the US Customs Bureau is filled with petitions from various industries complaining about the dumping of foreign goods, which costs US industrialists millions of dollars each year, it is reported from Chicago today that all grain bins in the US are suffering from an overflow of wheat. Regardless of the price, they are willing to sell as long as it is exported abroad. The prices of wheat and corn are so low that remote villages would rather use them as fuel than transport them to the market for sale. The price of corn in the US is currently only $14.50 per ton. In areas west of the Allegheny Mountains, the value of high-quality coal is still more than this amount, so farmers now believe that transporting corn to the market is a waste of labor and gasoline. It is better to use it as fuel, which can save the cost of transporting coal home. The vast grain bins set up by the US government are now filled with grain waiting to be exported, and sales prices are actually being negotiated. It is reported that several European countries have placed large orders with the US, so corn and wheat prices have risen slightly today. However, competition for export trade among several major wheat-producing countries is fierce, and it is feared that orders will decrease again after the market price rises slightly. According to agricultural experts, the world's wheat production is currently 1.2 billion bushels, while the world's demand is only 750 million bushels. With this huge surplus, wheat prices will definitely be difficult to rise for a while. Since the 17th century, wheat prices have never been as low as they are today. Therefore, although Americans deeply abhor destroying finished goods, this time they consider burning corn as firewood not surprising.

Japanese in Great Confusion After Su and Zhang Raise the Banner of Righteousness 58

▲ Fearing Danger to Japanese Residents

▲ And Guarding Against Soviet Union Involvement

▲ Military Certainty Lacking

▲ Efforts to Appease Ineffective

A special dispatch from outside the Pass (Guandong): Traffic between Harbin and Manchouli on the Chinese Eastern Railway has been cut in two since Man Hai raised the banner of righteousness on September 29th. Telephone and telegraph communications are completely severed. The Japanese are extremely anxious, concerned about the safety of their residents. However, aircraft cannot directly fly to Manchouli for reconnaissance. News from the Man Hai area relies on reports from the Soviet Consul in Manchouli, Strunov, to Blagoveshchensk, and then relayed from Blagoveshchensk to Vladivostok before reaching Harbin. Japan suspects that the Man Hai incident has some background involving the Soviet Union, but they dare not offend them at this moment. Firstly, they are concerned about the severed communications and the danger to the lives of their residents. Secondly, they fear that the Soviet Union might actually assist Su Bingwen and launch a large-scale offensive, making the situation even more serious. Therefore, although they are extremely dissatisfied with the Soviet Union, they dare not show it. Although the Kwantung Army headquarters has declared it will take decisive action, it has hesitated for many days, not daring to act immediately. On October 15th, three aircraft flew to Hailar, aiming to bomb the aircraft parked at the Chinese Eastern Railway's materials factory. This aircraft was shot down by Su Bingwen's troops at Qiqihar on September 28th while conducting reconnaissance over Manchouli. The Japanese military wanted to destroy it to prevent it from being used by the Soviet army. They dropped ten 50-pound bombs and fourteen 25-pound bombs, but none hit the target. Su Bingwen, fearing they would drop bombs on the city streets, ordered soldiers to drive out 30 Japanese residents and make them stand in the main thoroughfare. The Japanese aircraft, seeing their residents and fearing they would be affected, ceased bombing and left. They returned and reported to the Qiqihar headquarters, but there was no suitable solution. Therefore, they have been hoping to resolve the matter through political means, planning to deceive the residents into leaving and then taking military action. Matsuki Naohiro, the commander of the Japanese 14th Division, arrived in Qiqihar from Harbin on the 19th to prepare for military action. Meanwhile, he sent Jin Xianli (the twelfth son of Puwei), the puppet mayor of Qiqihar, to Hailar to persuade Su Bingwen to return to the puppet state, promising to pay the owed military expenses, etc. Jin Xianli planned to travel by plane on the 21st with two Japanese military staff officers. On one hand, the Japanese military gathered forces, one force heading directly south along the railway line towards Zhujia Kan and Nianzishan, but has not yet engaged in battle with Su and Zhang's troops. Another force, consisting of 6,000 cavalry and artillery, made a large detour around Nianzishan, heading towards Zhalantun, the location of the deputy headquarters of Zhang Dianjiu of the Northeast Army. In addition to actively deploying defensive measures, Su Bingwen maintained written communications, feigning compliance with the Japanese military. He also replied agreeing to the Japanese side sending Jin Xianli as a representative. However, the Japanese side, having detected that foreign military experts were assisting Su's army, laying landmines in the Xing'anling mountain passes, and constructing artillery positions in the Boketu Mountains to resist if Zhalantun could not be held, considered advancing on Man Hai to be extremely difficult. The Japanese side also discovered that Guo Daofu, the leader of the Mongolian Youth Party, was actively in contact with Su Bingwen, planning to establish a new regime in the name of the Bargu-Buryat Republic in the northwest of Hulunbuir. Recently, the Youth Party has sent many propagandists from the Hailar area, carrying affiliation documents to various Mongolian banners, requesting them to join. It is reported that over 5,700 Mongolian princes and chieftains have joined. The founding policy will imitate the Soviet Union's federal system, formed by a multitude of small republics. It is also expected that under the protection of the Soviet government, a republic will be formed by seven ethnic groups: Mongolian, Buryat, Solon, Han, Soviet, and Tatar. A constituent assembly will be held by December 25th at the latest to decide on the form of government. Su Bingwen seems to have agreed to this. With the Soviet Union providing guns and cannons, and the Red Guards under the guidance of Soviet military officers, have gathered 12,000 troops. Su Bingwen has ordered the abolition of the customs checkpoints on the Manchouli border, allowing free import of Soviet goods. The Soviet Transbaikal Railway has reallocated hundreds of railcars, divided into several trains, traveling between Man Hai. Therefore, traffic in the area is frequent, and Russian merchants and Mongols are very pleased. West of Hailar, there is a great atmosphere of development. The Japanese side, unable to obtain news from Man Hai, has telegraphed its military attaché at the embassy in Russia to enter and exit Manzhouli to gather information. Whether the Japanese military will advance westward will depend on the outcome of Jin Xianli's persuasion of Su Bingwen and the report from the military attaché at the embassy in Russia. As for traffic between Angangxi and Harbin, it has been cut off for many days due to the advance of Deng Wen's troops under Ma Zhanshan into the Anda station area.

Continued Dispatch from Outside the Pass: Jin Xianli, who was dispatched by the Japanese side to Hailar to persuade Su Bingwen and Zhang Dianjiu, was originally scheduled to travel by plane on the 21st with two Japanese officers. However, fearing that they would be detained by Su and Zhang, they dared not take the plane immediately. After multiple telephone consultations, Su Bingwen agreed to send a car to Zhujia Kan to receive them, meeting in Boketu or Hulunbuir. Early on the 22nd, Jin Xianli, together with two Japanese, departed. stating that they had received a telegram from the Soviet Consul General in Manchouli, Strunov, stating that he had received a reply from Su Bingwen in the name of Commander-in-Chief of the National Salvation Army, agreeing to consider the Japanese request to release Japanese residents relayed by the Russian Consul. The Northeast Army is organized very strictly, and even the slightest letter is not allowed to be secretly leaked out by good people. Therefore, the Japanese side has not been able to obtain detailed information about Su and Zhang's military strength. Pu Datong's troops in Baiquan have been reorganized into three brigades. Wu Tianzuo's brigade and Nan Tingfang's brigade of Pu's army are besieging Kedong. Over half of the 800 Japanese troops in the city have been killed in battle, and Captain Kuroda has also been killed. Hope for Resolution of Jiaodong Issue 59

▲ Han Expresses Willingness to Withdraw Defenses First If Liu's Troops Leave Shandong

Jinan Dispatch: The Jiaodong issue has gradually attracted attention from all sides since Han Fuqu telegraphed the Central Government to resign. Zhang Xueliang, Song Ziwen, He Yingqin, and Song Zheyuan, Chairman of Chahar Province, all sent telegrams to Jinan yesterday, urging Mr. Han to stay. Yu Xuezhong's representative, Li Junxiang, is still staying in Jinan. Han's representative, Liu Xizhong, went to Peiping (Beijing) a few days ago to report the recent situation in Jiaodong and Han's suffering of having to resign to Zhang Xueliang, Jiang Bocheng, and Song Zheyuan and other North China generals, which gained understanding from all sides. Recently, due to Jiang sending a telegram to Zhang Xueliang, instructing him to mediate the Jiaodong issue nearby, all details needed to be reported to Jinan. Liu returned to Jinan from Peiping this morning, and after getting off the train, immediately went to the Provincial Government to meet Han and report. Considering the importance of the matter, I specifically went to the Provincial Government to visit Han at noon to inquire about the details. Han said: Director Zhang (Xueliang)'s opinion is also that Liu's troops must be transferred out of Shandong, but in fact, Liu cannot be transferred until the Third Route Army withdraws its defenses. Therefore, Director Zhang intends to temporarily assign Yantai and Longkou to be garrisoned by a third party, so that Liu's troops can leave Shandong from these two places in the future. I completely agree with Director Zhang's approach. Originally, I had no grievances with Liu Ruxi, only for the sake of relieving the suffering of the people in Jiaodong. If Liu does not leave Shandong, the suffering of the people cannot be relieved. Therefore, I propose that the Third Route Army can follow orders and withdraw its defenses first, but (1) there must be a clear order for Liu's troops to leave Shandong immediately, (2) the people in Jiaodong must be able to live and work in peace. If both of these points can be achieved, the Third Route Army can withdraw its defenses first at any time so that Liu's troops can leave Shandong. Chief of Staff Jiang (Bocheng) is making great efforts to mediate this matter, and his intentions are very good. However, the three previously discussed measures: (1) The Third Route Army will withdraw to the west of the Wei River, (2) Liu's troops will not be stationed on the Yantai-Weixian line, (3) The administrative power in Liu's defense zone will be completely handed over, only the first measure was implemented, while the remaining two measures were not achieved. Therefore, I believe that the suffering of the people in Jiaodong cannot still be relieved, and the withdrawal of defenses still needs to be considered. Minister He (Yingqin)'s intentions are also very good, and the matter of withdrawing defenses is currently being discussed. Commander-in-Chief Jiang has sent Zhang Boying (Fang) to Jinan to discuss this matter. I have already sent a telegram to welcome him. Zhang is starting from Hankou this afternoon and should arrive in Jinan within two or three days. This matter will probably have a result soon. I have always believed that this is a small problem and it is not difficult to resolve. As for my resignation, various parties have sent telegrams urging me to stay, and I am grateful for their kindness. However, I have recently felt that the political responsibility is too burdensome and my personal abilities are meager and I am not up to the task. I always want to get rid of it as soon as possible. The telegrams from He Yingqin, Song Zheyuan, and others urging Han to stay are recorded below.
