However, at this time when foreign troubles are becoming increasingly urgent and the country's steps are becoming more difficult, all fellow soldiers should reluctantly take on difficult tasks. You are loyal to the military and the country and have always valued obedience. I still hope that you will maintain the Central Government's prestige with a spirit of concession and hope that you will not give up on overcoming difficulties. This is what I hope and pray. I arrived in Peiping from Zhangyuan on Yu Yang's day and have reported it. Song Zheyuan, Respectfully, Seal.

▲ Zhang Xueliang's Telegram: To Chairman Han Xiangfang, Brother Xunjian, Ma Dian has been received. Times are difficult and problems are endless. The overall situation in North China relies on our joint efforts to maintain. You have indicated that you are in a difficult situation and insist on retiring. Not only will the Central Government's intentions not allow you to retire, but my humble sincerity cannot bear to see you leave midway. In short, the facts are all there, and everyone can see them. Your difficulties will eventually be fully understood. I urge you not to be overly anxious and to dispel the idea of resigning. I respectfully hope that you will consider and adopt this. This is my greatest hope. Your Brother, Zhang Xueliang, Youzi, First Seal.

Provincial Committee Member Zhang Yue and Valley Ziliang, commander of the 22nd Division, previously received orders from Han Fuqu to go east from Jinan, passing through Weixian, Shahe, and along the Yantai-Weixian line, to inspect Yantai. On the return journey, they also passed through Longkou, inspected, and arrived at Shahe on the 25th, where they met Cao Fulin, commander of the 29th Division. This morning, they departed from Shahe and returned to Weixian, where they met Liu Shuxiang, Chief of Staff of the Weixian Headquarters. At 2:00 PM, they returned to Jinan by armored train, arriving at Jinan at 10:00 PM. Zhang told visitors that Yantai, Longkou, and the Yantai-Weixian line were all very calm, but business was quite sluggish. Liu's troops in Yexian were constantly thinking of breaking through, and they launched another attack outwards yesterday, but were repelled by the Provincial Army. It is reported that Valley and others are scheduled to visit Han tomorrow morning to report on the inspection. (October 26th)

Ministry of Railways Completes Plan for Yuehan Railway 60

▲ Scheduled to Open to Traffic in 1937

▲ Total Construction Cost Estimated at Approximately 60 Million Yuan

▲ Proceeding with Borrowing Boxer Indemnity Funds and Issuing Public Bonds

The Ministry of Railways believes that the unfinished Yuehan Railway has had a profound and significant impact on the transportation, commerce, and culture of the provinces of Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, and Guangdong. It has recently planned to complete the construction of this railway. However, during this time of national crisis, the central government's finances are particularly difficult. However, for the sake of the country's transportation future, the construction of this railway cannot be delayed. Therefore, it is proposed to borrow Boxer Indemnity funds and issue public bonds to raise funds. It is estimated that completing the entire Yuehan Railway project before 1937 will cost 60 million yuan in Chinese currency, equivalent to 3.76 million British pounds. The railway authorities plan to borrow 20 million yuan directly from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund and issue 40 million yuan in public bonds. The public bonds will be issued in Shanghai, China, and London, England, with the revenue of the Yuehan Railway used as collateral for future repayment of principal and interest. Gu Mengyu, the Minister of Railways, has already drafted detailed plans and has sent a letter to the Board of Directors of the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund for consultation. The original letter and plans are recorded below:

▲ Ministry of Railways Letter (Reply Required): With reference to your Board's Letter No. 943, which stated that the Board had resolved at its 11th Board Meeting on September 5th regarding the Ministry's proposal to borrow future Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Funds to serve as the fund for issuing Yuehan Railway public bonds, that this case is extremely important and that the Board could not object and would have the Chairman inform the Ministry of Railways to provide a detailed plan to the Board for discussion at the next meeting, the record has been made. A corresponding record has been made, and it is hoped that you will investigate and handle the matter and reply. We are submitting a proposal for borrowing future Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Funds to serve as the fund for issuing Yuehan Railway public bonds for your review and reply. This is addressed to the Board of Directors of the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund.

▲ Borrowing Boxer Indemnity Funds: According to the report of the British Boxer Indemnity Advisory Committee, the amount of Boxer Indemnity funds to be returned from December 1922 to 1945 is 11,186,547 British pounds. The Ministry should receive two-thirds, totaling 7,457,698 British pounds and some change. It is proposed to borrow this amount to complete the Yuehan Railway project. According to the engineering plan, the funds due from 1933 to 1936 will be directly borrowed and used. From January 1937 to December 1946 (originally until 1945, but due to annual suspensions of payment, it was moved to 1946), the future funds will be borrowed as a fund to issue public bonds, and the actual amount received will be allocated to the railway. Regarding the British Boxer Indemnity funds accumulated and due before February 1932, a contract has been negotiated and agreed upon between the Ministry and your Board to borrow and use the funds, either directly investing them in the Yuehan Railway or temporarily lending them to other railways first, with the stipulation that they be repaid and then re-borrowed by the Yuehan Railway. The unborrowed funds will still be requested for borrowing on time in the future to meet the needs of the Yuehan Railway project. Regarding all the British Boxer Indemnity funds to be received from January 1937 to December 1946, approximately 3,365,360 pounds, it is proposed to borrow them as a fund to issue public bonds. The detailed measures are approximately as follows: (1) The amount of public bonds to be issued will be based on the amount of British Boxer Indemnity funds to be received annually during the above-mentioned period, which is sufficient to repay the principal and interest of the public bonds. The total amount is set at 2.45 million pounds. (2) The location for issuing public bonds will be either in Shanghai or in London, or both, with the amount and date of allocation to be determined by the Ministry based on market conditions. (2) The actual amount received from the issuance of public bonds will be used to purchase materials in London at half the amount, in accordance with the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Exchange of Notes, with the remaining half used for the domestic needs of the Yuehan project. (4) The public bonds issued with the Boxer Indemnity funds will only pay interest during the Yuehan project period before 1936, which will be paid from the railway construction account. Starting in 1937, the principal will be repaid, and interest will be paid on the face value of the outstanding bonds, all of which will be paid from the British Boxer Indemnity funds due. (5) The aforementioned public bonds will be repaid in 20 installments over ten years from 1937 to 1946, with principal and interest repaid every six months. The amount of bond notes to be repaid in each installment will be determined by the Ministry in a list. (6) The order in which the bond notes are repaid will be determined by the Ministry by drawing lots at the time, according to the amounts listed in the table. (7) The face value of the bond notes will generally be listed in British pounds, and the principal and interest will also be calculated in British pounds. (8) The issuance of bond notes and the repayment of principal and interest will be managed directly by the Ministry or entrusted to other institutions. (9) The British Boxer Indemnity funds borrowed to serve as the fund for issuing public bonds will still be paid principal and interest in accordance with the usual practice, with the Ministry and your Board signing a contract and paying principal and interest in accordance with the repayment and interest guarantee measures stipulated by your Board. (10) Every six months, your Board will allocate two-thirds of the actual Boxer Indemnity funds received to the Ministry. After the Ministry receives the Boxer Indemnity funds, the repayment of principal and interest in the future will also be based on this actual amount received. (11) The Yuehan Railway will be used as collateral for the British Boxer Indemnity loan, and the Ministry will be fully responsible for it. Before 1936, during the railway construction period, the interest to be paid will be paid from the railway construction account. After the railway opens to traffic in 1937, the principal and interest to be repaid will be paid from the operating revenue. (12) The period for repaying the British Boxer Indemnity loan will be four to six years after the Yuehan Railway is completed and opened to traffic (approximately in 1937). For the convenience of calculation, or after all the British Boxer Indemnity funds have been borrowed, repayment will begin in 1947. (13) The principal of the aforementioned Boxer Indemnity loan to be repaid by the Yuehan Railway will be paid from the railway's operating revenue and will be repaid in 20 years. The amount of principal and interest to be paid before the principal is repaid and after the principal begins to be repaid will be paid every six months. (14) The silver dollars converted from the British Boxer Indemnity loan allocated to repay the principal and interest of the public bonds will be calculated according to the average telegraphic exchange rate in Shanghai or London on the day of allocation. In the future, the principal and interest of the Boxer Indemnity will be repaid in Chinese currency silver dollars. (15) The Ministry and the Board will exchange documents to inform each other of the silver dollars converted from the British Boxer Indemnity loan and the amount of silver to be repaid in each installment in the future, and a separate table will be drawn up.

▲ Explanation of the Plan: The uncompleted section of the Yuehan Railway is only the Zhuzhou-Shaoguan section. Among them, the section from Yunzhou to Lechang has already started construction and is nearing completion. The required funds will be budgeted separately. This plan is based on the Zhuzhou-Lechang section. According to the Ministry's recent estimate, the cost of completing this section is: (1) Construction costs: 27.5 million yuan, which is approximately 1,617,000 British pounds at a conversion rate of 17 yuan to 1 British pound. (2) Material costs: 2,145,000 British pounds. The total cost for both items is approximately 3,762,000 British pounds. The Zhuzhou-Lechang section is planned to be completed in four years starting from next year, with an average annual cost of approximately 940,500 British pounds. During the four-year period to complete the Yuehan Railway, the Ministry should receive Boxer Indemnity funds due (1933-1936) totaling 1,524,325 pounds, which will be directly borrowed and used to cover the costs of labor and materials for Zhuzhou and Lechang. Compared to the required amount, there is a shortfall of 2,237,675 British pounds. The interest of 5% to be paid on the aforementioned directly borrowed Boxer Indemnity funds during the project period will be paid from the construction account, totaling 139,188 pounds. Including the shortfall in labor and material costs, the total is 2,376,863 pounds. After the 26th year (1937), the British Boxer Indemnity funds due to be received by the Ministry are estimated at approximately 3,365,360 pounds, which will be borrowed to issue public bonds of 2.45 million pounds. At a 95% actual receipt rate, it will amount to 2,327,500 British pounds. The aforementioned public bonds will bear an interest rate of 6% during the project period, totaling 474,000 British pounds. The actual amount received from the public bonds allocated to the Yuehan project will be insufficient, and after deducting interest, there will still be a shortfall of 523,363 pounds, which will be allocated from the principal repayment item of the material purchase advances from various railways during the project period. According to the report of Wang Jingchun, the Ministry's representative, the accumulated funds in London from December 1912 to February of this year totaled 3,673,825 pounds, 14 shillings, and 4 pence. After deducting the various allocations to be made, the Ministry's share of two-thirds is 2,139,217 pounds, 16 shillings, and 3 pence. The amount that has been borrowed and is being negotiated for borrowing totals 1,310,000 pounds, leaving a balance of 929,217 pounds that has not been borrowed. The Xiang-E and Guang-Shao sections of the Yuehan Railway, in addition to the uncompleted Zhuzhou-Shaoguan section, both need to be renovated. It was originally planned to borrow 350,000 pounds of Boxer Indemnity funds for the Xiang-E renovation costs and 100,000 pounds of Boxer Indemnity funds for the Guang-Shao renovation costs. Xiang-E has already borrowed 110,000 pounds, and Guang-Shao has borrowed more than 30,000 pounds. Xiang-E needs 240,000 pounds, and Guang-Yun needs 70,000 pounds, all of which are planned to be allocated from the aforementioned accumulated Boxer Indemnity funds. The Ministry's share of the unborrowed accumulated London Boxer Indemnity funds is more than 929,000 pounds. According to the above calculations, after allocating 240,000 pounds for Xiang-E and 70,000 pounds for Guang-Shao, there should still be a balance of 619,217 pounds. The Jiao-Ji material purchase advance of 35 pounds and the capital ferry loan of 200,000 pounds should all be repaid before the 26th year in accordance with the contract provisions, which is appropriate before the Shao-Le section is opened to traffic. Therefore, the 520,000 pounds of insufficient funds for Yue could not be obtained. The uncompleted project cost of the Shao-Le section of the Zhuzhou and Shao section, which accounts for 1.5 million yuan in construction and material expenses, as well as debt repayment, is intended to be paid for this purpose. It is not included in this loan of 70 million, so the construction fund will now be only 800,000 yuan, and it is proposed that the Guang Shao Railway Bureau will provide assistance to provide the cost of the Shao Le segment's construction. If not, an additional 523,363 would not be obtained. In order to have the traffic as soon as possible, there needs to be 800,000 yuan. To solve this, it has been proposed to have a payment system. If the accumlated costs of the London Fund were not used, they could be made available by other returning loans. The plan is to have the funds back no later than December 26 and be paid with cash. (The budget tables are omitted)

Shanghai Merchants Bureau's Plan to Develop Northern Shipping Routes 61

▲ Setting Up a Branch in Qingdao

Qingdao Communication: The Shanghai Merchants Bureau, in order to expand its business, has established a branch in Qingdao and appointed Sun Zhenwu as the director. He arrived in Qingdao a few days ago to prepare for everything. According to Zhang Zhongguang, an employee of the bureau, the Shanghai headquarters considered Qingdao an important trading port in northern China, making it necessary to establish a branch. Therefore, Director Sun was specifically assigned to Qingdao to take charge of the establishment. The headquarters originally had nine river steamers and twenty-six ocean-going vessels (excluding those currently being built). All shipping routes are divided into the Nanyang (Southeast Asia) route, the Beiyang (Northern China) route, the Yangtze River route (also known as the Shanghai-Hankou route), the Hankou-Yichang route, the Sichuan-Hankou route, and the Hankou-Changsha route. The Nanyang route has six branches in Fuzhou, Xiamen, Hong Kong, Guangzhou, and Shantou. The Beiyang route has four branches in Yingkou, Tianjin, Yantai, and Qingdao. The Yangtze River route has fifteen wharves along the way and eight branches in Tongzhou, Jiangyin, Zhenjiang, Nanjing, Wuhu, Anqing, Jiujiang, and Hankou. After the official establishment of the Qingdao branch, it is planned to add two shipping routes: one from Qingdao to Shanghai, Shantou, Hong Kong, and Guangzhou, with three ships designated for this route: "Gongping" and "Meili" (both around 3,000 tons), and "Wu Yang" (about 5,000 tons). If shipping demand increases in the future and ships are insufficient, "Haiyang" and "Hairui" will be added to this route. The other route will run between Qingdao, Tianjin, Yingkou, and Dalian, with three ships temporarily designated for this route: "Xin Ming," "Xin Feng," and "Anning," specifically for transporting local products and goods. The internal organization of the Qingdao branch will be divided into four sections: business, general affairs, accounting, and documentation. Once the branch location is secured, it will move in for formal operation and commence shipping services. (October 26)

The Land Tax Assessment Turmoil in Jiangdu Has Not Subsided 62

Yangzhou Communication: The land tax assessment turmoil in the second district of this county has spread to the tenth district. Not only has the aftermath not subsided, but it also shows signs of expanding. In the tenth district, gentry and wealthy households whose houses were set on fire by villagers include those of District Head Lu Guangjian, Town Heads Xiao Jie and Xiao Zhenyang, as well as Si Tu Miao's Shi You'an and Tang Jinwan, Huang Jue Qiao's Wen Tongshun, Dou Yaozhai, Fang Yaoqing, Wang Xishou, Fangjiaxiang's Zhu Lianhe, Yijiaji's Wang Yongnian, Dou Sifang, Qilidian's Zhao Yongqing, Jijia Restaurant's Liu Hengyi, Yangjiamiao's Gao (surname), and others, totaling more than thirty households. All have reported to the county seat, which has forwarded the reports to the provincial government for instructions. A notice has been issued, roughly stating that the provincial government ordered a land survey and the Civil Affairs Department to reorganize the land, which overlapped. It has been resolved to have the Civil Affairs and Finance Departments review the matter. The county's previous request to approve temporary measures for the Finance Department to investigate land taxes should be suspended. All villagers should have no further concerns. It is also reported that groups of villagers are moving towards the ninth district. The county government has dispatched the fourth squad leader of the police force, Cheng Gongyu, and transferred forty-some police officers from the first and fourth squads to Xiangji Town to assess the situation. Coincidentally, Lin Zhaolong, the leader of the three propaganda teams sent by the county party headquarters to the Huaiqiao area to conduct propaganda, was tied up and beaten by villagers at Jijia Restaurant. Some team members escaped and reported to the independent regiment headquarters, public security bureau, and police team via telephone. Zhang Jifu, the supervisory committee member of the county party headquarters, led the police team to set off. Wang Yingzhang Zihe of the independent regiment also sent about a battalion, including a machine gun company, to continue their journey. En route, they encountered Committee Member Lin returning to the city in a small car. Upon inquiring, they learned that he had been rescued by the police team. Nearly ten thousand villagers were planning to surround the police team and were resisting. Committee Member Lin has been taken to the Tianye Hospital for treatment, and his injuries are not severe. It is reported that Liu Jinggao, whose house was burned down by villagers at Jijia Restaurant, saw two old men and one man in a Western suit among the crowd, using redwood sticks to direct the villagers and shouting to seize the police team's guns. Liu urgently used his self-defense pistol to kill one of the old men (another old man was stabbed four times by civilians). The police team captured the man in the Western suit and found a list and a police whistle on him. According to the man in the Western suit, his name is Luo Pijiang, and the deceased's surname is Chen. They have been escorted to the city for interrogation. Liu has also come to the city to identify the suspects. As for the detained villagers, after interrogation on the afternoon of the 26th by Li Mingyang, the director of the security bureau, and Han Deqin, a member of the provincial government, three people were released on the spot, and seven were released on bail. On the morning of the 27th, another seven were released on bail. Tang Qibin, Wang Xiaomazi, Zhu Qicai, and others are still in custody. On the evening of the 26th, Director Li and Committee Member Han convened a meeting at the River Works Bureau with the heads of the first, second, third, and fourth districts, as well as the heads and deputy heads of the respective towns, to discuss the matter. The district heads and others presented two points of view: (1) to request the issuance of a proclamation to temporarily suspend the land survey; (2) to request leniency in granting bail to the detained villagers. Li and Han stated that the first point was related to central government policy and could not be approved without authorization. The second point would be considered after investigation. On the afternoon of the 27th, Li and Han also invited representatives from various agencies and groups to discuss the matter. Committee Member Han reported on the causes of the turmoil, and Director Li reported on the differences between the situation in the morning and afternoon. Chang Shizhi, a representative of the Chamber of Commerce, and Ge Jianshi and Zhou Shaochang, members of the Provincial Party Headquarters, expressed their opinions successively. Finally, Li and Han announced that they had submitted a request to the provincial government to deal with the arrested villagers leniently. Currently, the gates of Yangzhou City, including the Guangchu Gate and the Northwest Gate, remain closed in the morning and partially open in the afternoon. (October 27)

Yangzhou Continued Report: Yesterday, after the police team went to the countryside and captured Luo Pijiang and others and brought them to the county, Provincial Government Member Han Deqin and Security Bureau Director Li Mingyang interrogated them that evening. According to their confessions, they revealed the names of their accomplices and masterminds. The police team, detective team, and public security detective team were immediately ordered to go to the countryside overnight to search and arrest them at their addresses. From then until this morning (28th), Ge Guangxing (also known as Ge Dayan), Liu Jinju, Yang (surname), Jiang Tingbao, Jiang Tingyan, Jiang Tingkun, Chen Youshan, Chen Yongsheng, Chen Yongcai, and Bu Dengchang, Liu Yushan, and others who were captured with the help of the public, totaling more than ten people, were escorted to the city. County Magistrate Yang, together with the two provincial committee members Han and Li, conducted a detailed investigation from 8:00 AM until evening. The security was tight, and details were unknown, but it was heard that the suspects were heavily implicated. This morning, villagers were still gathering at Jijia Restaurant, with even more people than yesterday. Around 10:00 AM, they attempted to riot and set fire to houses again. The third battalion of the independent regiment, which had been sent to suppress the riot, fired a volley into the air, and the crowd dispersed. They then gathered again at Yangjiamiao and Qilidian. Upon receiving the news, the city sent battalion commander Shen of the independent regiment with two companies of soldiers to suppress the riot. It was reported that around 4:00 PM, more than ten thousand villagers gathered at Tan and other places behind Nongweitian and advanced towards the Jijia Restaurant area. Upon receiving the news, military and police units dispatched teams to various locations to strictly defend and search for the ringleaders. The city's order is better today, but the soldiers and police guarding the city are paying close attention to pedestrians. The Public Security Bureau has also sent police to inspect hotels day and night, questioning anyone with suspicious behavior. The independent regiment has also sent teams to patrol the streets. Provincial Committee Members Han and Li believe that the seven detained villagers, including Zhu Qicai, are only slightly suspected due to the land tax assessment turmoil, and their circumstances are forgivable. Today, they ordered the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce to provide bail for their release. (October 28)

The Ministry of Finance Revises the Business Tax Regulations of Jiangsu Province 63

The Provisional Business Tax Regulations of Jiangsu Province were previously drafted by the Finance Department, passed by the Provincial Government Council, and submitted to the Ministry of Finance for record-keeping. The Ministry of Finance, considering that the three-tier tax rate stipulated in the regulations was based on the precedent in Zhejiang Province, has recorded it together with the organizational rules of the Business Tax Bureau and the regulations for supervisory commissioners. It seems that the clauses of the regulations have been revised with discretion and submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval. The revised clauses are extracted below: (Article 2) All businesses operating within Jiangsu Province, except factories that have already paid factory tax to the Central Government, limited liability banks that pay income tax, and industries designated as tax-exempt by central government laws, shall pay business tax in accordance with the provisions of these regulations. (Article 4) Among goods sales businesses, those that specialize in wholesale and do not engage in retail sales may be taxed at half the business tax rate. If there are retail sales operations and wholesale operations are also conducted, the tax shall be levied uniformly in accordance with the regulations. (Article 8) Businesses shall keep the following account books and be prepared for personnel dispatched by the Business Tax Bureau to investigate at any time: (1) Goods Purchase Book, (2) Goods Sales Book, (3) Daily Cash Receipt and Payment Book, (4) Monthly Total Book, (5) Annual Total Book. (Article 10) The business tax rates levied in this province shall be temporarily set at 5 per mille, 8 per mille, and 10 per mille of the total business income or business capital, respectively. The types of tax rates shall be specified in a separate table. However, industries that have been designated for tax reduction by central government laws shall still be taxed at the reduced tax rate. (Article 12) When the Business Tax Bureau investigates the total business income and business capital of a business, it shall inspect various books and documents from the previous year and this year. If there is any pretext for evasion or refusal to present them, or if the presented documents are false, in addition to penalties in accordance with the regulations, the tax may be estimated and levied according to the actual business situation. (Article 18) The business tax shall be paid by the business according to the amount of tax payable (directly to the Business Tax Bureau, or collected directly from the shops by personnel dispatched by the bureau on a household basis. It shall not be contracted by any trade association or individual. Anyone who violates or obstructs this shall be strictly investigated. (Article 26) Businesses that engage in the following behaviors shall be punished separately: (1) Failure to establish account books in accordance with the regulations, (2) Refusal to declare or submit to investigation, (3) False declaration or avoidance of heavy taxes, (4) Concealment and failure to report, hoping to evade taxes, (5) Concealment of books and documents or forgery of accounts and vouchers. (Article 27) Businesses that engage in the behavior described in item 1 of Article 26, i.e., failure to establish account books in accordance with the regulations, shall be fined between one yuan and ten yuan. (Article 28) Businesses that engage in the behavior described in item 2 of Article 26, i.e., refusal to declare or submit to investigation, shall be subject to compulsory execution in addition to a fine of between one yuan and twenty yuan. (Article 29) Businesses that engage in the behavior described in item 3 of Article 26, i.e., false declaration or avoidance of heavy taxes, shall be ordered to pay the supplementary tax in addition to a fine of between one and three times the amount of tax payable. (Article 30) Businesses that engage in the behavior described in item 4 of Article 26, i.e., concealment and failure to report, hoping to evade taxes, shall be ordered to pay the supplementary tax in addition to a fine of between three and five times the amount of tax payable. (Article 31) Businesses that engage in the behavior described in item 5 of Article 26, i.e., concealment of books and documents or forgery of accounts and vouchers, shall be fined between five and ten times the amount of tax payable. (Article 35) The Business Tax Investigation Certificate and the Business Tax Receipt and Fine Receipt shall be numbered and issued by the Finance Department and shall be affixed with the seal of the respective Business Tax Bureau. The aforementioned Business Tax Investigation Certificate shall be in triplicate, and the Business Tax Receipt and Fine Receipt shall be in quadruplicate. One copy shall be given to the business, one copy shall be submitted to the Finance Department, one copy shall be kept by the Business Tax Bureau for record-keeping, and one copy of the remaining receipt shall be posted. (Article 40) These regulations shall be implemented after being discussed and resolved by the Provincial Government and submitted to the Ministry of Finance for review and approval by the Executive Yuan for record-keeping.

The Jiangsu People's Food Adjustment Association is Established 64

▲ Passed Articles of Association and Elected Committee Members

The Jiangsu-Shanghai People's Food Adjustment Association held its inaugural meeting at the Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce at 4:00 PM yesterday (28th). Thirty-four representatives from various counties attended. Qian Sunqing was publicly elected as the temporary chairman. The following matters were resolved: (1) The name was determined to be the Jiangsu-Shanghai People's Food Adjustment Association. (2) The Articles of Association were revised and passed. (3) The Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Shanghai Municipal Local Association, the Jiangsu Provincial Farmers Bank, the Zhenjiang Provincial Capital, the Wuxi Chamber of Commerce, and the Wu County Chamber of Commerce were elected to form a committee to preside over the association's affairs. (4) A request was submitted to the provincial government to order all counties to instruct the warehouse management committees to fully store accumulated grain funds for relief purposes. The Red Bandits in Western Anhui Have Been Suppressed 65

▲ The Fourth Division is Concentrated in Bengbu Awaiting Orders

▲ All Sectors of Bengbu Welcome Xu Tingyao

Bengbu Communication: Xu Tingyao, the commander of the Fourth Division, was ordered to lead his troops from Bengbu in early June to suppress the Red Bandits in northern Anhui. After arriving at Zhengyangguan, he launched an offensive against the bandits. Before long, he successively recovered key areas such as Xindianpu, Huoqiu, Hekouji, and Yejiaji. Subsequently, he was ordered to advance towards western Anhui to suppress the remaining bandits, and he continued to occupy places such as Damaidian and Mapu. The Red Bandits on the Anhui border were then suppressed. The division then stationed in Jinjiazai, settled the refugees, searched for hidden bandits, and handled local rehabilitation. The Bandit Suppression Headquarters has now issued an order to the Fourth Division to return to Bengbu and concentrate to await orders, as the bandit atmosphere in the Henan-Anhui border area has been quelled. After receiving the order, Xu Tingyao ordered all units to return by train from their defense areas. He himself departed from Jinjiazai a few days ago. Yesterday (26th) afternoon, Xu, along with Independent Brigade Commander Guan Linzheng and several guards, arrived in Bengbu along the Huai River by small steamer. This morning (27th) around 2:00 AM, Public Security Bureau Director You Kaiyun and others led the security team, the water patrol team of the security bureau, and the citizens' self-defense corps to the riverbank wharf to welcome them. Xu arrived in Bengbu at 6:00 AM and was greeted by the troops. Xu then went to the Jiaotong Villa on Erma Road to rest. Representatives from all sectors and local figures visited in an endless stream. All stores in the city displayed banners to welcome him. According to Xu, the division's arrival in Bengbu is to concentrate and await orders. The defense area of Jinjiazai has been taken over by three regiments of Wang Jun's troops. On the same day, representatives from various agencies and groups held a welcome meeting at the Third Public Education Hall under Bengshan Mountain at 3:00 PM in the afternoon. Xu arrived at the meeting by car. Hundreds of people from all walks of life attended. Xu took the stage to give a speech, reporting in detail on the suppression of bandits in northern and western Anhui. He said that after setting out, it took three months to eliminate the Red Bandits on the Anhui border. There are now no bandits along the road from Huoqiu to Yejiaji and Jinjiazai, and pedestrians

can travel without worry. The Red Bandits in western Anhui have been completely suppressed. After the meeting, representatives from all sectors held a banquet for Xu and Guan Linzheng at the Dadong Villa at 6:00 PM in the afternoon. The host and guests toasted each other and were extremely cordial. Brigade Commander Guan reported on the Fourth Division's bandit suppression situation during the banquet. At 8:00 PM, the host and guests dispersed in high spirits. Xu took the Pingpu train to Beijing around 1:00 AM at night to meet with Chairman Chiang in Hankou and report on the bandit suppression situation. His troops have all departed from Jinjiazai and Yejiaji and will arrive in Bengbu successively in the coming days. (

October 27)

The Anhui Audit Office Implements New Regulations 66

▲ Salt Stores Must Provide Guarantee to Obtain Licenses

Wuhu Communication: The Anhui Provincial Salt Affairs Audit Office recently suddenly changed its regulations, issuing a notice to all salt-selling stores in the province, requiring them to provide a guarantee and apply for a license before November 1st in order to sell salt. It also ordered them to fill out a four-column list with the daily sales and inventory of salt and report it to the office. Failure to comply will result in the suspension of salt distribution. As a result, salt merchants across the province have protested and repeatedly sent representatives to negotiate with the Salt Affairs Audit Office, requesting consideration of commercial interests and avoidance of disputes. The Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation also sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance and the Salt Affairs Department, pleading on their behalf. At the same time, it sent a letter to the Salt Guild, asking them to inform all salt merchants to continue distributing salt as usual to maintain the people's food supply until further notice. Today, an emergency meeting was also convened at the County Chamber of Commerce. Everyone agreed that the new regulations issued by the Anhui Audit Office, requiring a guarantee and the creation of a list, have no precedent to follow. It is said that other provinces do not have such measures. How can Anhui be different? It was decided to send another telegram to the Ministry of Finance, ordering the Audit Office to continue to operate under the old regulations

in order to reassure the business community. However, according to the Audit Office, the Transportation Bureau used to charge 1.5 yuan to 4 yuan for each license, but now it has been decided to charge nothing. Therefore, a guarantee is required to show restriction, and the tax police inspection of various sub-salt stores can be abolished to avoid disturbances. All counties in Anhui have already implemented this, except for Wuhu. As for the daily reporting of the four-column list, it is the implementation of scientific audit measures. Since the business community complains about the inconvenience, it has been decided to change it to monthly reporting. As for the concern that salt stores may oppose it, leading to a lack of salted food, that is not a problem. At the appropriate time, the Audit Office can immediately conduct public sales by region, and the people's food supply will not be affected. In view of this, the attitudes of both sides are firm and deadlocked. It is difficult to predict how it will be resolved. (October 28)

Local Communication

Songjiang 67

▲ Autumn Assessment of Fineness Generally Reduced by 0.1%. The County Government Previously Issued a Notice to All Agencies and District Heads, stating that the fineness of this year's autumn assessment should be discussed and decided as soon as possible to serve as a basis for reporting. A meeting was convened today, presided over by County Magistrate Shen. The situation of this year's autumn assessment was reported. After detailed discussion by the attendees, opinions were divided. After summarizing and voting, it was decided that the fineness of this year's autumn assessment would be generally reduced by 0.1%. ▲ Record of Court Hearing for the Bankruptcy Case of Songjiang Bank. The bankruptcy case of Songjiang Bank was heard again by the County Court yesterday. Zhang Zuo Liu and others, representatives of the plaintiffs, and lawyers Liu Zhimou and Qu Yue, appeared in court to state that the case has been delayed for more than

months and should be subject to provisional attachment to prevent difficulties in future enforcement. Subsequently, Sha Xunyi, the defendant's lawyer, argued that Zhang Shengshan, one of the defendants, is currently seriously ill, and the implementation of attachment would exacerbate his illness. Moreover, the defendant's lawyer Tang Mingshi was absent today, and the start of the debate should be postponed. The plaintiff Zhang Zuo Liu rebutted this. The court ruled that the debate hearing would be held on the 21st of next month and ordered everyone to withdraw. Zhang Shengshan, the ailing defendant, had already died last night (28th).

Nanhui 68

▲ Supporting the Northeast Volunteer Army. A discussion meeting was held by various people's groups in this county a few days ago, and it was decided to organize a donation team to support the Northeast Volunteer Army. The County Party Headquarters selected instructors for each team and printed propaganda materials, donation receipts, and flags for each team. All of these were completed yesterday and were immediately distributed to various people's groups and instructors to prepare for departure. At the same time, an order was issued to the party headquarters in each district, and a letter was sent to the county government to instruct the local government in each district to assist in the fundraising efforts.

▲ Uncle Stabbed and Injured by Nephew. Zhu Xiaodi, a farmer from Pengqimiao, recently prevented his nephew Zhu Laisheng from picking cotton

flowers in the field, resulting in an argument. Suddenly, Laisheng stabbed Xiaodi with a knife, inflicting six wounds, and blood flowed like a river. It was a tragic sight. Xiaodi's wife, Su (surname), filed a complaint with the county government to request an examination of the injuries and detention of the perpetrator. Laisheng was taken into custody. Yesterday (October 28th) afternoon, auditor Hu Cheng held a court hearing. Zhu Xiaodi was unable to move due to his serious injuries, and his wife, Su (surname), appeared on his behalf to describe the attack by her nephew Laisheng, requesting strict punishment. The defendant Zhu Laisheng was brought from prison. After the interrogation, the court ruled that the charge of harming a collateral relative was established and ordered a sentence to be announced at a later date, and the defendant was ordered to be returned to custody.

Wuxi 69

▲ Arrest of People from Haimen for Impersonating Officials and Inspecting Japanese Goods: Ni Shiyan and Shi Fanghua, recently purchased fifty-four and a half pieces of "chou huo" (goods from enemy countries) broadcloth and thirty-four bolts of remnant fabric from Yufu East Store in Shanghai. They loaded them onto a wheel-operated vessel to Wuxi. On the afternoon of the day before yesterday, at 10 PM, they arrived in Wuxi and hired a small barge belonging to Sun Sanda at Tonghui Bridge, intending to transport the goods to Luoshe Town for sale. Unexpectedly, three men wearing Western suits, namely Lian Zhengming, Zhang Song, and Hua Jinfa, appeared. They carried forged official documents and insignia, claiming, "We are recorders from the Third Detachment of the Sixth Brigade of the Second District of the Waterborne Provincial Public Security Team. We are ordered to inspect Japanese goods and contraband." After speaking, they leaped onto the boat, intending to inspect the goods, and said that it would cost one hundred yuan in foreign currency to settle the matter. Ni and others realized that they were impersonating public officials, engaging in intimidation and fraud, and acting extremely unlawfully. They reported the matter to the Fifth Branch of the Public Security Bureau for investigation. Upon receiving the report, Director Peng immediately dispatched Patrol Chief Chen and police officers to bring Lian and the others to the bureau. Bureaucrat Ji Yaping conducted an interrogation. Yesterday, a document was prepared and submitted to the General Bureau for review. Furthermore, Fang Jinsheng, a shareholder and manager of the Beitang Dahexing Company, as well as Yunhua Cloth Store, Beidajie Tongtaichang, Tang Ruicheng, Tianjin and other stores, have recently been privately importing large quantities of "chou huo", altering their appearance, expanding sales, and deceiving customers. This matter was discovered by the Blood Soul National Salvation Corps, who sent a letter of warning.

They were given three days to respond in the newspaper. If they continue to transport and sell these goods, the most severe measures will be taken against them.

▲ Dispute Between Officials and Merchants Over Slaughter Tax: Since Xu Jigong took over the local slaughter tax, officials and merchants have been arguing over the tax amount, resulting in disputes for over a month without resolution. Director Xu believes that the Meat Industry Association is clinging to old habits, misunderstanding the law, obstructing rectification, and attempting to reduce the tax amount. The County Chamber of Commerce convened a meeting of meat merchant leaders on the eleventh of this month to mediate and invited industry leaders again on the eighteenth to persuade them. Subsequently, the industry representatives replied that due to the current economic decline and sluggish business, they could not afford the previous tax amount. However, because it concerns special funds for education, they must reluctantly fulfill their obligations, but both tax collectors and merchants must be considered. They have acknowledged and paid half of the special construction tax and will be allowed to pay one-eighth of the special construction tax in installments thereafter. After reading the letter, Director Xu considered the language vague and empty. He noted that during the previous mediation by the Chamber of Commerce, a three-way agreement was reached for a daily payment of 69.3 yuan in regular and additional taxes. Now, the association's response to the Chamber of Commerce disregards the special funds, stubbornly adheres to its opinions, and delays the matter. Therefore, he has resubmitted the matter to the County Government, requesting that it forward the letter to the County Chamber of Commerce for review and action.

▲ Dispute over Sales Boundaries of Refined Salt: The Wuxi Jiuda Refined Salt Company has had repeated disputes with the Anti-Smuggling Merchant Patrol Team over the boundaries of its sales area, which have remained unresolved for a long time. The company complained that the Wuxi merchant patrol repeatedly seized official salt and imposed arbitrary fines. It submitted a petition to the Salt Affairs Administration, requesting that it order the return of the original salt, compensate for the losses, protect the rights of the people, and emphasize taxation. A reply was received stating that according to the investigation by the Songjiang Transportation Deputy, the refined salt seized by the merchant patrol was outside the boundary. It was requested that the salt be returned to the original sales location in accordance with the general rules for refined salt, as required by the order. At the same time, the Salt Transportation Deputy Commissioner's Office received instructions from the Ministry of Finance, stating that regarding the dispute over the sales boundaries of Jiuda Refined Salt in Wuxi, instructions were received from the Executive Yuan stating, "Although Wuxi's commercial port does not have a clearly defined boundary, the county has stated that, based on past commercial conditions, the prosperous roads from Jingyun in the east to Kaiyuan in the west within the county seat can be considered as natural boundaries of the commercial port. Following the precedent of Nanjing's sales of refined salt, where the scope was based on the former Pingzheng Yuan's ruling, with Xiaguan as the boundary, the area should be designated as the sales area for refined salt in Wuxi. Both parties should be ordered to comply to show restriction and prevent disputes." The Transportation Deputy Commissioner's Office has ordered the Jiuda Company to comply. However, the Anti-Smuggling Merchant Patrol Team argues that the boundaries of the commercial port were clearly defined after a long period of discussion by the former Commercial Port Bureau and the former Wuxi City Board of Directors, and there are diagrams to prove it. There is no way to mix it with the newly constructed roads. They have submitted separate reports to the Ministry and the Executive Yuan to fight for their case.

▲ Joint Defense Office Issues Notice on Early Winter Defense: The joint defense of Wu, Kun, Qing, Jiang, Song, Jin, Wu, Xi, Yi, and Jiu counties decided at the previous meeting in Wuxi that, due to local unrest and the importance of defense, winter defense should be implemented earlier this year. It is stipulated that it will last for five months, from November 1st to the end of March next year, following the established practice. However, the waterways are particularly unstable this year, and a water patrol team should be organized, with red and green lights displayed at night. Green lights indicate peace, and red lights can be used in case of an accident to call for assistance from other teams. During the winter defense period, railway stations and ports should be strictly investigated to prevent petty thieves from mingling in and disrupting public order. If refugees arrive, passports should be suspended and original passports canceled and sent to the provincial government for disposition and return to their original places of origin. The presence of communists within the territory should be closely guarded against to prevent accidents. The above items were notified by the Joint Defense Office to the County Government yesterday, ordering the land and water police to comply.

Jiangyin 70

▲ Problem of the Chengxi Road Occupying Farmland: The Chengxi Road has been occupying farmland for three years since it was built and opened to traffic. The Construction Bureau has not yet surveyed the land. Village chiefs of Xinmin, Jiyi, Weishan and other villages have proposed to the First District Office that, since the land has been occupied, not only has the land price not been paid, but also taxes must still be paid, which is extremely unfair. The County Government should be ordered to expedite the survey and first exempt the land from taxes and give land prices to remove people's worries. The District Affairs Meeting yesterday (the 27th) decided that District Chief Liu should submit the issue to the District Chief Meeting for discussion.

▲ Arson Fugitive Apprehended in Suzhou: After the arson case involving Chen Zhangba and Wang Xiaoda in the Second District was solved, the case of assaulting the police and the robbery case at Chen Minghe's house in Liuwei were also solved one after another with the capture of key criminals. Because accomplice Fei Quanyuan was hiding in a distiller's shop in Loumen, Suzhou, Detective Team Leader Huang went to Suzhou to arrest him and brought him back to Cheng on the 27th. He confessed to being a lookout during the arson at Wang Xiaoda's house and was immediately taken into custody.

Changzhou 71

▲ Party Headquarters Requests Strict Handling of Corruption Case in the Court: The Supervisory Committee of the Wuyi County Party Headquarters believes that since the establishment of the County Court, the handling of cases has been unsatisfactory in many ways. Even Lei Renlong, as the President of the Court, has committed three crimes of dereliction of duty, fraud, and embezzlement. Recently, a clerk named Ni Yuzhang dared to openly bribe Judge Hu Jingqing with regard to the serious offender Wang Zeng'ai Zhu, who was charged with poison. Both cases have been separately judged and investigated. Yesterday (the 27th), a special report was submitted to the Provincial Party Headquarters and forwarded to the Ministry of Judicial Administration, ordering the Higher Court to thoroughly rectify and strictly handle the matter according to the law.

Abduction of Village Chief Solved in Shanghai: The village chief of Jinnu Village in the Fourth District of Wuyi and the young son of Zong Xigen were kidnapped by bandits Zhang Hongsheng and Chen Ergen. Several suspects, including Zhang Rongzhao, were subsequently apprehended. Recently, Ni Gusheng, the captain of the county detective team, learned that Zhang Hongsheng and others were hiding in Shanghai. He immediately led his team to Shanghai overnight and arrested Zhang and Chen on the spot in a Yidao Jiao teahouse. They were sent to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau for detention. Meanwhile, the county government prepared a document and went to Shanghai on the 29th to retrieve them for trial.

▲ Verdict on Riot Case by the High Court: Jin Xiangsheng and others, who were involved in the November 18 riot in Wuyi last year, appealed to the High Court after being sentenced by the County Court. After repeated interrogations and prosecutions, the verdict was announced on the afternoon of the 28th. Jin Xiangsheng's sentence was reduced to ten years of imprisonment. The other four, Zhu Yuanpei, Zhang Chengguan, Ye Jinde, and Yu Yiqin, were found not guilty and acquitted. However, Jin Xiangsheng still declared his dissatisfaction in court and filed an appeal.

Changshu 72

▲ County Defense Committee Expands Publicity: The Jiangsu Provincial Defense Committee and the Department of Civil Affairs instructed all counties to conduct expanded defense publicity campaigns to raise public awareness. It is reported that upon receiving the order, the County Defense Committee scheduled the period from the 24th to the 29th of this month as the expanded publicity period. It requested various agencies and organizations to cooperate in accordance with the provincial publicity guidelines. County Chief and General Commander Tan Yigui, together with Public Security Bureau Chief Yin Peng, Education Bureau Chief Yu Cheng, Head of Corps Affairs Wang Kunshan, and other committee members, carried a large number of publicity materials and went to various districts for practical publicity. In advance, they telegraphed the district chiefs and district corps chiefs of each district to convene the chiefs of each jia (unit of ten households) to gather at the district office and await dispatch. On the appointed day, the general commander and others first explained the main points of the publicity to the jia chiefs in detail, and then the jia chiefs went to various townships and towns for publicity in order to achieve universal coverage.

Rugao 73

▲ Triplets Born: In Fengjiazhuang, Northwest Township, Matang District, there is a Ge family. The wife, Zhang, is nearly fifty years old and has no children. This spring, she was heavily pregnant, suspected of having dropsy. Yesterday, she gave birth to three sons, all of whom are very lively.

Nantong 74

▲ Guerrilla Team Pacifies the Sea: Shen Fengshan, the leader of the Jiangsu Provincial Security Team's maritime guerrilla team, was ordered to lead his troops out of Lvsi to pacify the sea area infested by pirates. They advanced in two routes, north and south. The bandits between Qidong and Yancheng have been scattered and it is expected that they will be cleared within half a month.

▲ Joint Land and Water Defense in Tonghai Qidong: Due to unrest caused by bandits, the county heads and representatives of military and police agencies of Nantong, Haimen, and Qidong counties decided to implement joint land and water defense. Wooden fences will be set up at key intersections between the counties, and security police will be stationed to be responsible for opening and closing the gates and investigating. All coastal ports along the river and sea will be guarded by water patrol teams. During the winter defense period, all remote small ports will be temporarily closed.

It is reported that the Jiangyan Chamber of Commerce has already forwarded the letter.

Gaoyou 76

▲ Shareholders of Egg Company Arrested for Defrauding Funds: The Dingda Egg Company outside the North Gate of the city was established by Zhu Yaoqing, Yang Daoqiu, and Luo Haiquan with joint investment. Zhu was from Huaian City and had been in the egg business for a long time. He served as a comprador in the You Post Branch of the Peilin Company in Shanghai. However, Zhu was naturally frivolous and was not trusted by the head office, so the local branch in You was closed. This spring, Zhu joined forces with Luo and Yang and raised three thousand yuan to organize the Dingda Egg Company. The business was developing well. In order to develop the business, Zhu also added a branch in Huaiding and had dealings with money shops such as Yuanhe in the county to facilitate turnover. Unexpectedly, the previous time there was too much inventory in Shanghai and the price of eggs plummeted, resulting in a significant loss. Recently, Zhu and the others suddenly had a whimsical idea. Using the name of collecting eggs in Huai, they successively defrauded more than 18,000 yuan from money shops such as Yuanhe and Dingyuanchun. The three of them divided the money. Yang returned to You the day before yesterday and temporarily hid at home. Zhu and Luo also planned to escape by boat. However, the money shops detected this and reported it to the police. The police arrested Zhu and Luo and sent them to the Huaian County Government for interrogation. They also confessed that Yang Daoqiu, who was on the run, was hiding in Gaoyou. The Huaian County Government ordered the police to come to You by car overnight and arrest Yang. They were escorted back to Huaian yesterday (the 26th) for interrogation.

Jiading 77

▲ Bandits Li Zheng and Lü Xirong Executed by Firing Squad: After the capture of bandit leaders Li Zheng and Lü Xirong in the major kidnapping case in the Northeast Township, they were repeatedly interrogated. Due to their repeated offenses of kidnapping for ransom and conclusive evidence, the County Government sent a telegram to the Provincial Government for review and approval. After receiving the provincial telegram, the two bandits were executed by firing squad according to law. The criminals were then taken to the execution ground after their identities were verified.

Huzhou 78

▲ Corruption Case in District Office Relief Distribution: In the Seventh District of Changxing County, when distributing relief rice, the clerks and secretaries of the district office secretly sold the rice. When the villagers became aware of this, they secretly reported it to County Chief Wang, who went to investigate and verify the matter. He took the clerk Shi to the county and the secretary Zhu fled in fear of punishment. District Chief Sun Hongdu was dismissed because he was unable to restrain them. Shi has been sent to the County Court for investigation and handling. Secretary Zhu is currently being pursued.

Pinghu 79

▲ Judicial Police Disrupt Theater: This county has never had a county-run fire brigade. Local merchants purchased water dragons and established a fire-fighting association, which has always been known for its enthusiasm in fire-fighting work. Recently, due to lack of funds, they negotiated with the Gongle Company to temporarily use the Xinmin Theater and hire actors from the Zhangji Stage for several days to raise funds. After several days of performances, the box office was not good and they lost about 300 yuan. On the fourth day, the weather was fine and the box office was very good. Unexpectedly, when collecting tickets, it was discovered that four law enforcement officers from the county government, Ge and Pu, were occupying first-class seats without buying tickets. When asked to explain, they slapped the ticket collector, Lin, several times and shouted to open fire, causing great disorder. The audience dispersed. The members of the fire-fighting association were furious, believing that the county government neither established a fire brigade nor condoned the lawless law enforcement officers who came to disrupt the event. The fire-fighting association could no longer be maintained, and they could only ask the county government to take on the fire-fighting duties. They telegraphed each fire station, ordering them to carry the water dragons to the county government. In an instant, the horns blew and each water dragon rushed to the county, causing great alarm among the citizens. Later, a patrol officer from the Public Security Bureau detained the law enforcement officers who caused the incident and telegraphed Tang Yuanbo, an official from the fire-fighting association, to persuade them. The turmoil subsided.

Hangzhou 80

▲ Deadline for Rice Merchants to Settle Pledges: The banking and money industries in Hangzhou have accepted over 100,000 shi of rice pledged by rice merchants last year, with loans amounting to no less than 600,000 yuan. The deadline for settlement was generally set at the end of April this year. However, since the beginning of summer, rice prices have been declining, and the pledgers have adopted a wait-and-see attitude and ignored the matter. After autumn, rice prices became even cheaper, and the previous pledges became increasingly unmanageable. On the other hand, new grains are entering the market, and merchants need to borrow from banks or money shops to finance their operations. The banking and money industries refused to accept new pledges because the previous loans had not been settled and were in the process of being urged to be settled. After a month of stalemate, the matter could not be resolved. The City Chamber of Commerce decided to convene a meeting of leaders from the banking and money industries and rice merchants on the afternoon of the 28th to discuss a solution. Over twenty people attended, with Jin Runquan presiding. After repeated discussions, it was decided that the first step would be for the Chamber of Commerce to send letters to the Provincial Chamber of Commerce and then to the chambers of commerce in various counties and towns related to rice pledges, urging rice merchants and other pledgers to quickly come up with a plan to settle the rice pledges before November 15th of this year to maintain credit. It was also decided that the Chamber of Commerce would send letters to the banking and money industries associations, informing their members to continue accepting rice pledges as usual to benefit the people's food supply.

Educational News Highlights

Foreign-Run Schools Must Not Conduct Religious Rituals 81

The Ministry of Education previously received a report from the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau regarding the Huaxia University Bible School and its primary school department promoting religion, requesting instructions. The Ministry of Education has ordered the bureau to instruct the school to comply with the regulations for private schools. (Article 5 of the regulations for private schools stipulates that if a private school is established by a religious organization, religion must not be a compulsory subject, religious promotion must not be conducted during class, and students must not be forced or induced to participate in religious rituals in the school. Religious rituals must not be held in primary schools.)

Funds for Tianjin and Beijing Colleges from February to June Still Difficult to Supplement 82

The Executive Yuan recently instructed the Ministry of Education, stating that the request from the Joint Association of Faculty and Staff of Tianjin and Beijing Colleges to withdraw the order not to supplement the educational funds from February to June of this year should still be handled in accordance with the previous resolution of the Executive Yuan (funds cannot be supplemented; during the national crisis, all national schools follow the same procedure).

Fourth Annual Elementary School Joint Sports Meet Concludes: Wanzhu Wins Both Men's and Women's Track and Field Championships 87

▲ Group exercises of each school have improved... Awards were given yesterday afternoon

Yesterday was the third day of the Shanghai Fourth Annual Elementary School Joint Sports Meet, which was also the last day of the sports meet, the award ceremony, and the closing ceremony. Most of the boys' track and field events were finals on this day, so the students of each participating school were extremely excited. —Grand Award Ceremony— 90

At four o'clock in the afternoon, during the award ceremony, autumn rain pattered down. However, the crowds of elementary school students remained packed together. Boy Scouts cordoned off an area in front of the stage to serve as a standing area for the winning athletes and school representatives receiving awards. In addition to the medals prepared by the organizing committee, which were awarded immediately after the final of each event (those who didn't receive them can collect them from the office), the remaining prizes were displayed on the stage: silver shields, silver tripods, satin banners, and mirror frames, a dazzling array. After the music and salutations were completed, Director Pan of the Municipal Education Bureau delivered a speech on behalf of the Mayor, praising the participating students for their vibrant spirit and the proficiency of their group exercises. Next, Chief of the Organizing Committee Ma Chonggan reported on the distribution of this year's championships. Then, names were called and awards were presented until the lights of every household began to glow. The meeting concluded with music.

Yesterday's Western League Football Match: Youyou vs. Donghua Dramatic Battle 105

▲Unfortunately, a Crushing Defeat of 1-3

▲First Half Dramatic Battle with No Result

The Donghua and Youyou football teams played yesterday in the rain at the Chinese Baseball Field. This was a scene from the Western League Football Group A league. Youyou knew it was no match, so it conserved all its strength to defend. In the first 45 minutes, Donghua could not find a way to break through, wasting its efforts and achieving nothing. Instead, Youyou almost ambushed Donghua, but fortunately, Zhou Xianyan saved it skillfully, preserving the territory. In the second half, Youyou's defender and main player, Zhu Qiu, was injured, and the formation suddenly became scattered, allowing Donghua to take the opportunity to score two goals successively by Tu Kaiyuan and Feng Yunyou. Later, Youyou's Shi Jinsheng also returned one goal. Donghua's Li Yichen also scored one goal. As a result, Donghua won 3-1. There were few spectators, and the performance was not very exciting.

▲Donghua Missed Two Shots After three o'clock, referee He Chunhui ordered the kickoff. Youyou's kickoff could not go deep and was fiercely pressed by Donghua. Youyou saw that the situation was not good, so the forwards were all transferred back to defense, not taking the offensive. Donghua's Chen Yutian and Chen Hongguang got the ball under Youyou's goal, with excellent opportunities, but unfortunately, they did not score.

▲The Iron Gate Unbroken, Fortunately Youyou only attacked with three people from the left and right wings and the center forward (the two inside forwards both defended), so there were few attacking opportunities. However, there were two dangerous shots that almost broke Donghua's iron gate, causing the audience to gasp. One was Zhu Shengfa's pass to the center, with Dong Xiaopei heading the ball towards the corner of the goal. Zhou Xianyan quickly saved it. The other was Sun Hupei's solo advance on the left wing, breaking through two lines of defense and sending the ball in front of Donghua's goal at the baseline. Dong Xiaopei rushed up, Zhou Xianyan received the ball and fell to the ground, but fortunately, he rolled away, averting the danger. These two shots greatly startled Donghua. Neither side scored in the first half.

▲Main Player Injured, Territory Falls Donghua was determined to win and tried every possible way to defeat the enemy from the start of the afternoon, but for the first 15 minutes, there was still no opportunity. Later, Youyou's defender Zhu Qiu was injured in the thigh and could not control the enemy, allowing Donghua's Tu Kaiyuan to score a goal in the chaos, opening the scoring. Afterwards, Feng Yunyou also scored a goal, and Youyou's territory was lost.

▲Shi Jinsheng Breaks the Iron Gate Youyou knew that defending was useless after losing two goals, so it launched an offensive, advancing on the right wing, forcing a corner kick. Zhu Shengfa made a wonderful pass, and Ben Ningyuan became a corner kick. Zhu Zaixi landed right in front of the goal, and Li Ning headed the ball to clear the danger, but unexpectedly, it was obtained by Youyou's midfielder Shi Jinsheng. Shi had an excellent opportunity at this point and shot at the goal, with the ball entering the corner of the goal. Zhou Xianyan fell to the ground but did not reach it, and the iron gate was broken. However, not long after this goal, Donghua's Li Yichen made a fierce shot, which was clear and beautiful, resulting in a score of 3-1. The lineups were as follows:

▲Donghua

Li Ning, Tu Kaiyuan, Wan Xianghua, Chen Hongguang

Zhou Xianyan, Feng Yunyou, Li Yichen

Guan Xun'an, Wu Youliang, Chen Jiaqiu, Chen Yutian

▲Youyou

Sun Hupei

Zhu Qiu, Lu Shi, Hu Youcheng

Liang Guanlian, Wang Shusen, Dong Xiaopei

Qian Yaobin, Shi Jinsheng, Xi Qiaosheng, Zhu Shengfa

Little turbulence in finance and gold markets 110

▲Yesterday, the gold market had slight fluctuations, initially weakening and then strengthening. The high and low prices differed by six taels during the day, with twists and turns of more than two taels in the middle. In the end, it continued to fall by one tael. Dealers were optimistic, but the price fell immediately at the beginning of the morning, mainly due to the sharp decline in the silver market in the UK and the US, especially due to the sudden surge in silver futures and private telegrams on the Silver Exchange. As a result, the price broke through the 750 tael mark. Fortunately, the demand from various firms exceeded the supply, so the price gradually rose, and the exchange rate rose by half a point. The gold price hovered around 50 taels. Later, the British gold turned from strong to soft. Although some hedgers sold, the banks continued to buy. It was also reported that the Central Bank bought another 420 bars of spot gold, priced at 52 taels. It is said that Yuanxingyong and Dadecheng offered the price, which boosted confidence and made the price more attractive. As a result, the price stood between 53 taels. One hundred and forty bars for November were dropped by Ruixing, and the long positions of Duofang, Tongfeng, and Heng were short three taels. Because the market is closed on Saturday and to check the market conditions this week from the quiet to a lively atmosphere, waves are surging. At the beginning of the week, it was weak due to the rise in silver prices. The minimum was 739 taels and two qian. Afterwards, the exchange rate plummeted, resulting in a situation where the exchange rate was strong in the UK and soft in the US. In addition, the gold market was surging with buyers, and gradually advancing. After that, it suddenly broke through the 760 tael mark, reaching 61 taels and two qian. Unexpectedly, international news was unfavorable to the gold market, so it fell sharply. By the end of the week, it had returned to within 50 taels. The difference throughout the week was 22 taels. Compared to last Saturday, it still rose by eight taels. However, the state of wavering is very difficult to predict. The market conditions yesterday are recorded below.

▲Initial weakness, followed by recovery The opening price for December was 748 taels and three qian, a drop of five taels and five qian, which was actually affected by the sharp rise in the silver price of eight fen and five li and the private telegrams. The long-term price also rose by more than seven li, so the final price was 47 taels. Hengxing bought more than 100 bars, and Ganfeng, Yongru, Decheng, etc. followed, immediately pulling up two taels and eight qian, to 49 taels and eight qian. The exchange market initially appeared loose. The current exchange rate against doing 198125 is 10 pence in January. Then, HSBC absorbed US$875, but at 9:15, some retail investors sold, suppressing the price by a small amount. Then, US$0.0625 per month was available for sale, and Zhifeng, Yongzhaochang, Hengyu, and Ruirenxing, acting for Qiao Ribu and others, came in, and then returned to 50 taels, totaling 51 taels. When HSBC quoted higher exchange rates for British and American currencies by 125, it immediately fell back to 49.5 taels. Chang, Dadecheng, Futaiheng, etc. bought, and HSBC absorbed 75 British gold in November, adding two taels, to 51 taels and five qian at 10:00. At that time, it was reduced by another two taels, as Hengyu, Yuantai, Yuanmao, Yongru, etc. sold. Subsequently, there were fluctuations of several qian. After 10:30, the Central Bank absorbed 75 US dollars in November, and Fuchang, Dadecheng, Senchangyong, etc. bought, jumping more than two taels, to 52 taels and five qian at 10:50. Hengxing suddenly sold, immediately plummeting more than one tael, to 50 taels and seven qian at 11:00. Later, Yuanxingyong entered the market to buy, and it was rumored in the market that the Central Bank opened a cash position, which boosted confidence and immediately rose two taels, to 52 taels and nine qian at 11:30. At this time, there were also many sellers, instantly decreasing one tael and five qian, to 51 taels and four qian. After 11:40, banks absorbed 875 US dollars in December, 9375 in January, and Zhaofeng, Changyifengyong, and goods for hedging came to mirror and drag in, causing the price to rise again by one tael, to 52 taels and nine qian at noon. When the market closed at 12:00, it was 52 taels and four qian, and it was done again to two taels, which was bought by Yuanmaoyong, etc. However, Ruixing released about 200 bars at this time, which had been entered in the morning (presumably Ribu’s notes), which was one tael lower than the previous day (according to the listing). The maximum for half a day was 52 taels and nine qian, and the minimum was 47 taels, with a review of five taels and nine qian. The red bar then fell, adding twenty taels and a half, because it was heard that Yang Qinghe Jiuji had stopped business and sold the stock to close the business.

▲Listed price less depressed two taels The listed price of the US dollar was higher by 125, so it was 814 taels, counting 64 taels. Later, 623 taels, and then 64 taels again. The result was 61 taels, less depressed by two taels than the previous day. Logged for November 54 taels, December 52 taels, and make up the water 55 taels.

▲A glimpse of the transaction There were more buyers on the table. According to statistics, Dadecheng, Zhifengyong, Yifengyong, Zhaofengchang, Yuanmaoyong, Futaiheng, and Yuanxingshui. Fuchang all entered. Ruixing initially entered and then exited, for a total of more than 600 bars (presumably Ribu’s notes). Shunli, Bingxing, and Fuyu retail investors all exited. US dollar hedgers entered. Hengyu, Yuantai, Daxingyong, Hongkangyong, Hengchangyong, etc. were busy with deposits and withdrawals. The Ningbo gang exited for more than 400 taels, entering a small number. The Cantonese gang, Hengxing and Yifeng, entered a total of more than 200 taels, and exited a total of more than 300 taels. The total number of bars for customer trading by each firm was more than 22,000, and there were still more than 3,000 for November that had not been settled.

Hunan Rice Continues to Rise — Fujian Merchants Vigorously Buying, Price Up Half a Dime — 111

Yesterday, imported rice sales to local customers were not brisk, with only slight inquiries. The market remained stable, but Hunan rice was very popular among the Fuzhou merchants. Their inventory had been exhausted, and new shipments were quickly purchased by them. Yesterday, 236 bags arrived, which were entirely bought by the Fuzhou merchants. Prices rose by half a dime compared to the previous opening. 100 bags of Hunan machine-oiled rice were priced at $9.20, and 136 bags of machine-milled Jing rice were priced at $8.95. 200 bags of Number One Saigon rice were sold locally for $9.00, it is said.

Flour and Wheat Plunge Wildly — Hit by the Exceptionally Cheap Imported Wheat —

▲ Yesterday, the flour market, after the morning opening, showed signs of near-term stability but distant-term decline. Imported wheat prices varied slightly. The current month was supported by a major mill despite two price reductions. Therefore, although initially sluggish, it ultimately remained stable. Far-term months experienced a decline of over one dime due to unfavorable news about imported wheat. Bullish traders exited, and mills also offered their holdings. By the afternoon opening, except for the current month, which remained stubbornly firm, the other months saw an unprecedented plunge. The price of Australian current wheat was rumored to be as low as $3.50, and the Fu and Fu factories each had orders for one or two ships. Consequently, mills were eager to sell after pricing, with Fuxin alone reportedly selling 550,000 bags. Today's trading volume reached around 1.2 million, the highest since the market opened. The minimum market price for far-term one-two months fell to $1.73. This record is not only newly created but also rarely seen in over a decade. The overall trend is due to the pressure from surplus overseas, and there is little hope for future gains. As a result, the current month was better by 1.25 cents, November fell by 1.5 cents, December fell by 3.5 cents, January-February fell by 4.25 cents, and March fell by 3.25 cents.

▲ Yesterday, after the morning and afternoon openings, wheat futures largely showed a plunging trend. Imported wheat prices fluctuated little, but the overseas news was very gloomy. The eagerness to receive imported wheat increased, revealing an oversupply of agricultural products. If the local market does not follow the trend, future pressure will intensify. Therefore, the situation was unfavorable at the opening, and the afternoon was even more subdued. However, trading was minimal, and development was difficult. As a result, December fell by four cents compared to the previous day, and January, February, and March each fell by three cents. The delivery of current wheat was unaffected, wheat prices first fell then rebounded.

New Fungk Foreign Firm Reports: Chicago wheat on Friday (the 28th) first fell due to good Argentine harvest reports, then rose due to strong Canadian wheat. The total trading volume on the 27th was 20 million bushels. Overall, the future of wheat is still uncertain, but the selling pressure seems to have ended. A rebound within the day is expected.
